Customs Suspends Salvage of Sunk Ship, Plans to Bomb It 150

The Norwegian "Kinnaird" ship, which sank several months ago due to a collision on the Pudong Lujiazui side of the Huangpu River, has been abandoned by the ship's company. The Customs authorities believe that the masts and smokestacks protruding above the water surface obstruct navigation. They had planned to salvage the ship, but due to the ship's large size, at least seven or eight large iron barges would be needed for buoyancy, and large machinery would be needed to lift it. However, the ship has been submerged for a long time. Even if it were salvaged and sold, the proceeds would not be enough to cover the salvage costs. Therefore, the Customs authorities have abandoned the salvage plan. The work of pumping water from each cabin with water pumps has also been stopped. The only remaining solution is to bomb it.

After being discovered by West Xun, the captain was immediately informed, and McPherson was sent to the Country Hospital by ambulance. He died at 4:40 PM. The cause of the suicide is being investigated.

Apprentice Killed by Freight Truck, Wang Changxian Died 152

Wang Changxian, an 18-year-old apprentice from Zhenjiang at the Minsheng Socks Factory on Minquan Road in the French Concession, went to the Tiger Stove in Panjia Lane in the Chinese district across the street with two hot water bottles at 8:30 PM last night. As he was walking in the middle of Minquan Road, east of the Wireless Station, a freight truck with a Public Concession license number 16800 and a Municipal license number 13175, traveling eastward, sped past. Wang could not avoid it and was knocked to the ground. The wheels rolled over his body, covering him in blood, and he died instantly. The truck saw the accident and sped away. The police officer on duty blew his whistle and chased the truck to near the Old North Gate, where it was apprehended. The truck driver, Chen Erlin, and the truck were taken to the Chenxiangge Police Station for questioning. The truck driver, Chen Erlin, was detained for investigation. It is reported that the deceased's parents are still alive in his hometown. He came to Shanghai last month to learn his trade at the factory and had only been there for thirteen or fourteen days. Lin Baofang, Who Surrendered Himself, Denies Running Gambling Houses 153

Lin Baofang (aka Ling Baofang), nicknamed "Rotten Neck" Baofang, had been running large gambling houses with Tang Sunfu, Qian Zongfan, and others in the Hongkou area. After the police arrested his accomplices Hong Yongfan (Chuan Chunfa, Wang Ruifeng, etc.), the First Special District Court issued an arrest warrant for Lin. Recently, Lin, knowing that he could not hide any longer, hired a lawyer and surrendered himself to the Jiaxing Road Police Station last week. Chinese Detective Shao Jingfan detained him. The situation of the First Special Court's interrogation and detention has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Huang Risheng of the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court continued the interrogation. The police lawyer Zhang Shizhu charged Lin with operating a gambling house. Then, Chinese Detective Bu Shiting of the Laozha Police Station testified that when he arrested the gambling house criminal Fu Chunfa, Fu confessed that the large gambling house was operated by Lin Baofang and led them to Dou Pai at No. 24 Yongxiang South Lane, Xian Road, but Lin was not found. Chinese Detective Zhao Lianbi of the D'Isigny Road Police Station testified that after arresting Hong Chengfan, Hong confessed that the gambling house in Hongkou was jointly operated by Lin, Tang Sunfu, and Qian Zongfan and led them to Lin's house to arrest him, but he was not found. Judge Huang also presented the files of previous criminals. The descriptions of Wang Ruifeng and others matched Lin's appearance and build. He questioned Lin Baofang, who firmly denied running any gambling houses, claiming that he was being framed. After the lawyers of Lin and the police exchanged arguments, the court decided to announce the verdict on Friday. Lin was returned to custody.

Dispute Over the Death of an Adopted Daughter-in-Law, Older Sister Claims Abuse by Parents-in-Law, Cause of Death Awaits Autopsy 156

Tang Xiaolong, an eight-year-old girl from Yancheng, was betrothed to Ding Guangyou, a fellow villager living at No. 400 Magilu, a packer of rickshaws, several years ago by her parents as his future wife. During the January 28th Shanghai Incident, the girl's parents were both killed by stray bullets, so the girl was raised by her older siblings. Ding was allowed to bring the child to his home last year. In the first month of this year, the child suddenly became ill and died on the evening of the 30th of last month. Her older sister Jiang Tangshi (living at No. 12 Chang'an Road, Zhabei) heard about this and believed that her younger sister's death was caused by abuse by Ding and his wife. She reported this to the Gordon Road Police Station, which sent Chinese Detective Liu Chunshu to investigate and detained Ding Guangyou. The child's body was taken to the Renlu Forensic Examination Office. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the office to examine the body. The Western policeman first reported the previous incident and stated that Ding Guangyou had requested detention. Ding Guangyou confessed that he was 33 years old, and the deceased was his future wife and cousin. She was sent to his home by her brother last year, and she was already very thin when she came. In the first month of this year, she suddenly became ill and was bedridden. He had hired a doctor to treat her, but it was ineffective, and she died. She was both his future wife and his sister's daughter, so he treated her very well and there was no abuse. The two broken skin areas on her buttocks were caused by lying in bed for a long time and rubbing against the sheets. The older sister, Jiang Tangshi, stated that she was 17 years old and the deceased was her younger sister. She was sent to Ding's house by her second brother last year. After arriving at his house, Ding and his wife abused her younger sister very severely, often beating her, not allowing her to eat enough, and there were two bruises on her buttocks as proof. Last year, when she met her, she told her that she was being abused. Now she does not know how she died, so she is requesting justice and a detailed examination. Guo Jun stated that he could not determine the cause of death from the deceased's appearance. He ordered that an autopsy should be performed, and the hearing would be adjourned. The body was handed over to the older sister, Jiang Tangshi, to prepare the coffin.

Wusong Branch Line Issues Discounted Group Tickets 158

The Traffic Department of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways issued a notice to all stations yesterday, stating: To facilitate group travel, starting today, group tickets can also be issued according to regulations between stations on the Songhu Branch Line and stations on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Lines. When calculating fares, the fare of the Songhu Branch Line should be added to the fare of the two main lines, and then discounted according to the group discount methods stipulated in Articles 40 and 41 of the Passenger Transport Regulations. However, groups traveling only between stations on the branch line will not enjoy preferential discounts if the price of each person's third-class ticket is less than five dimes after the discount. Stations on the branch line that have not applied for blank group discount tickets and group certificates should quickly apply to the accounting department for use. The notice is hereby issued for compliance.

Public Security and Public Utilities Bureaus Issue Proclamation Prohibiting Kite Flying, Due to the Danger of Obstructing Electric Current 160

It is springtime, the weather is sunny and breezy, and children often fly kites in various open spaces. The Public Utilities and Public Security Bureaus of this city believe that this activity is prone to danger and jointly issued a proclamation to ban it yesterday. The original text reads: For the matter of proclamation, flying kites can easily obstruct electric wires, leading to danger. Minor incidents can cause power outages, while major incidents can cause electric wires to fall, endangering lives. If not strictly prohibited, the harm would be unimaginable. This Public Security Bureau, to maintain public safety, and this Public Utilities Bureau, to maintain the electrical business, jointly issue this proclamation. Hereafter, flying kites is prohibited in any location near any electric wires. Those who deliberately violate this will be arrested by the police without leniency. This proclamation is issued for compliance. At the same time, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau has also asked the Public Security Bureau to stop it in order to maintain traffic and security.

Coincidence: Strange Birth Records: One Birth, Three Sons, Red, White, and Black; One Body, Three Colors, Green, Red, and Blue 161

Geng Jinsong, a 37-year-old man from Danyang residing at 7 Changyuan Lane, Xilinjin Road, Ximen, makes a living selling beef noodles at Fangbang Bridge. He married a fellow villager, Ms. Lu Yumei (34 years old). After marriage in their hometown, the couple had a harmonious relationship and had five children together, only one son and one daughter survived. Geng and Ms. Lu came to Shanghai last year. At around 9:00 PM on the 29th of last month, she suddenly gave birth to triplets, with their faces being red, black, and white, respectively. The reporter visited yesterday to verify the facts. The firstborn was a red-faced boy with a purple tinge. The next boy was black-faced, with skin similar to that of a piglet. The lastborn was a white-faced boy, as white as lamb's fat. It was truly [difficult to describe]. Because the delivery was not smooth, the black-faced infant died on the spot. However, the red and white-faced boys were very lively. The second landlord of the house and general neighbors claimed to be [unclear] Liu [unclear] Zhang reborn. Unexpectedly, at around 9:00 AM the day before yesterday, the red and white-faced boys also died one after another.

Zhu Guobao, from Huai'an, Jiangsu, lives in a straw hut under the bridge on Qimei Road and makes a living selling used goods. His wife, Ms. Chen, was pregnant for twelve months. At around 4:00 AM last night, she suddenly felt abdominal pain and was about to give birth. Her husband, Guo [unclear], accompanied her to the Pingmin Obstetrics Hospital in Hongkou, requesting delivery. She gave birth at 11:20 AM the next morning. The child was born without a sound and was about to die. Its head was green, its abdomen was bright red, and its hands and feet were blue. It weighed more than twenty pounds, looking like a three or four-month-old child. Dr. Wang of the hospital used surgery and injections to revive the child. Both the mother and child are now safe and sound and are still resting in the hospital.

The 228th inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of this bank on March 30, 1935. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 92,694,871 silver dollars, including 85,677,997 silver dollar notes and 7,016,874 subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of convertible note reserve is 92,694,871 silver dollars, including 73,694,871 silver dollars in cash reserve. The cash reserve includes 69,942,072 silver dollars stored in the issuance vault of this bank, 1,939,074 silver dollars stored in branch offices in various ports, and 1,813,725 silver dollars stored in peer banks. The guaranteed reserve is equivalent to 19,000,000 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 373,324.7 customs gold dollars. The total amount of the customs gold convertible note reserve is 373,324.7 customs gold dollars. The reserve includes 7,351.95 taels of standard gold, which is equivalent to 373,324.7 customs gold dollars at the fixed price of 50779. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's convertible note regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guaranteed reserve is 40%. The inspection results show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guaranteed reserve is less than 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is hereby issued. April 1, 1935, Ji Fuxun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Supervisors Xie Mingdong, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilun.

Pudong National Arts Research Society Established 165

Qin Dunfei, Cai Wenen, Sun Wenjin, and others, considering that Pudong's national arts have a long-standing reputation, but in recent years, due to a lack of contact, it has gradually been lost, which is regrettable, have organized the "Pudong National Arts Research Society" in Shanghai to establish contact and arouse the enthusiasm of fellow villagers to jointly improve. After preparations, it has now been established. The simplified charter of the Pudong National Arts Research Society is recorded as follows: (Name) The name of this society is the Pudong National Arts Research Society. (Purpose) The purpose of this society is to connect the feelings of fellow villagers, explore national arts, and improve health. (Qualifications) Anyone with good character and a legitimate occupation who has a foundation in national arts, regardless of age or gender, can join the society as a member of this society. (Subjects) Research in Shaolin, Tai Chi, wrestling, and other subjects. (Fees) A miscellaneous fee of one yuan is charged every six months (temporary donations may be made if insufficient). (Organization) A standing committee of nine members is established, elected by the members' meeting. (Duties) One standing director, one accountant, two administrators, four communicators, and one document clerk are appointed by the standing committee (all volunteer positions). (Time) Every Tuesday and Saturday from 7:00 PM to 9:00 PM. (Address) Temporarily located at 80 Gufuli, Baoshan Road, Zhabei. (Supplementary Provisions) Imperfect parts of this charter can be amended at any time with the proposal of more than half of the members.

He requested that I write a letter on his behalf to make a correction. Zhang Weiliang and Zhang Dong had a family quarrel over trivial matters in February of this year, but there was no physical violence or assault. After Zhang Dong's side misunderstood and filed a lawsuit, the First Special District Court advised them to withdraw the case. At that time, this lawyer defended Zhang Weiliang and witnessed the settlement of the case. Since then, Zhang Weiliang has not resented this. When Zhang Dong was due to give birth, Zhang Weiliang was still fully responsible for taking care of everything and providing expenses. On the 18th of last month, another lawsuit was filed due to other reasons. In fact, it was still a misunderstanding on the part of Zhang Dong, and the details were minor. There were no facts as reported in your newspaper. Fearing that readers would not know the truth and would affect Zhang Weiliang's personal reputation, I am sending this special request to be published in your newspaper to make a correction. To the Editor of Shenbao, Lawyer Shen Junru, April 1st.

Special Announcement

Yingcheng Bank's Business Report for 1934 (19) 174

The total number of yarn factories in the country this year is 136, with 92 Chinese factories, 41 Japanese factories, and 3 British factories. The number of spindles is 4,731,146, an increase of 119,789 spindles compared to the previous year. Among them, Chinese factories account for 2,742,754 spindles, accounting for 57.97%, and the increase in spindles is 105,341, accounting for 87.9% of the total increase. There are a total of 440,434 thread spindles, of which Chinese factories account for 143,024 spindles (32.47%). There are a total of 42,834 looms, of which Chinese factories account for 20,926 looms (48.85%), all of which have increased compared to 1933. Although the environment is not good, in order to survive, the yarn factories can only struggle with perseverance. The trend of shutdowns or reduced work has not decreased due to the increase in the number of spindles. According to the statistics of the Yarn Factory Association, the number of spindles shut down in the first half of this year increased by 104,933 spindles compared to the second half of last year, and the shutdown time was about four weeks. Reduced work has increased, and inventory has decreased. At the same time, yarn prices have fallen, and transactions are still booming. The total for the year is 319,923 bales, an increase of 334.87% compared to the previous year.

(2) Silk Industry The silk industry was the most sluggish this year. Taking Shanghai as an example, of the original 112 silk reeling factories, only two barely started work at the beginning of the year due to the decline in the silk market. When the spring cocoons started, the overseas silk market showed some activity, and the silk factories gradually started work, but only 33. During August and September, the overseas silk market plummeted, and Japanese silk was actively devalued, and silk prices became more sluggish. After the silver export tax was levied, there was a brief period of excitement, but it was also sluggish due to poor sales. At the end of the year, only 15 or 16 factories were operating. In other places, such as Wuxi, the most prosperous time this year was no more than 33 factories, and only ten or so factories were operating in Xiaoshan, Jiaxing, Haining, and other places. The situation in Sichuan and Guangdong was also declining, and the scene was bleak. The silk weaving industry shared the same fate. Taking Shanghai as an example, there were still 387 silk factories in 1933, with more than 4,780 looms. This year, only about 300 factories were struggling to maintain operations, with 2,500 looms, a decrease of about one-half. Bankruptcies of silk and satin shops were also heard from time to time. The decline of the silk industry can be seen in general. (To be continued)

Instigator in the Tang Jiapeng Case, Wang Xinggao Sentenced to Life Imprisonment, Zhao Guangfu Leaked Secrets in Letter to Wife, Recantation Fails and Escape Plan Thwarted 176

Tang Jiapeng, formerly known as Tang Ayu, the manager of the Great World amusement park in Ningbo, was ambushed and shot to death by thugs hired by his enemies at around 1:00 AM on June 17th, 1933 (i.e., the morning of the 18th), as he was leaving the Great World with three or four friends and about to board his car. At the same time, a passerby, Wu Guangcai from Yangzhou, a bathhouse attendant, was killed by stray bullets. The murderers fled the scene immediately. Two months later, the Special Bureau of the French Concession police arrested two accomplices, Zhang Tinggui (nicknamed Xiao Sizi) from Funing and Zhao Guangfu from Yangzhou, in various locations on Haifang Road in western Shanghai, and recovered the Browning pistol used to kill Tang. They were sent to the Second Special District Court for prosecution. After three trials, Zhang was sentenced to 20 years imprisonment and Zhao was sentenced to life imprisonment and sent to prison. Recently, the French police, based on a tip from the prisoner Zhao Guangfu, continued to pursue the main offender, Wang Xinggao (also known as Wang Xiaogao) from Funing (40 years old, residing at No. 46 Menggu Road, Zhabei), who was a detective in the Shanghai Public Security Bureau at the time, at 11:30 PM on December 13th of last year in Room 537 of the Central Hotel on Guangdong Road, with the assistance of Chief Detective Lang Boli, Chinese Detective Wang Rusong, and Detective Guo Shaorong. He was taken back to the police station, transferred to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and investigation. As a result, he was prosecuted for premeditated murder under Article 284 of the Criminal Code. Judge Xiong Huiping held several hearings to investigate the case and requested the Hubei Higher Court to investigate Wang's tenure as a warden at the Hubei First Prison in Wuchang. However, Wang consistently denied involvement in the murder and hired a lawyer to defend him. However, Zhao Guangfu testified in court that Wang was Wang Jinkui. Later, Judge Xiong was transferred to the Higher Third Branch Court, and Judge Sun Peng took over the case for renewed trial. Zhao Guangfu suddenly recanted, claiming that Wang had an affair with his mistress and he was framing him out of spite. However, Wang's family persuaded Zhao's wife to negotiate a settlement. In a letter that Zhao wrote to his wife in the detention center, teaching her about the settlement, the letter was intercepted by the authorities and submitted as evidence by the police. Witnesses were also gathered and interrogated, and the proceedings were concluded. The date for sentencing was set. As reported earlier, Judge Sun came to the First Criminal Court at 10:00 AM yesterday, ordered Wang Xinggao to be brought to the court, briefly questioned his name, age, and origin, and then announced the verdict. Wang Xinggao was sentenced to life imprisonment for instigating premeditated murder and was deprived of his civil rights for life. During the appeal period, the defendant will remain in custody in the detention center.

Various Organizations Write to the Public Works Bureau to Protest Telephone Price Increase, Requesting Consideration of Taxpayers' Interests and Cancellation of the Approved Price Increase Proposal 178

The First and Second Special District Citizens' Union of this city, the National Goods Promotion League, and other organizations yesterday wrote to the Public Works Bureau of the Public Concession and the Board of Directors of the French Concession to oppose the telephone price increase, and requested that they demand a reduction from the telephone company on behalf of the taxpayers based on the contract provisions. The original letter stated: "To whom it may concern, the Shanghai Telephone Company has recently requested your bureau to increase user fees starting from April 1st on the grounds of high expenses and insufficient dividends. Such unreasonable behavior is opposed by all users, both Chinese and foreign. Our associations believe that your bureau, as the highest authority in managing the administrative security of the concessions, should consider the interests of the taxpaying citizens and curb such absurd actions that violate the regulations of public utilities. However, we are disappointed that your bureau has listened to one-sided arguments and has essentially accepted the principle of changing the fee structure, even slightly. Telephones are a means of transportation and are related not only to the business of taxpaying citizens but also to public security matters such as police and fire services within the concessions. Although the company holds the authority to operate exclusively, it must still consider the interests of the public. The company's economic reasons, as it claims, are nothing more than the high cost of improving equipment and the failure to achieve a full dividend. However, the company should prepare for improving equipment and developing its business. If the expenses are too high, it should reduce usage fees so that the number of phones can gradually increase, and revenue can naturally increase. It is neither fair nor wise to have existing users bear the cost of equipment that has already been used. As a result, the number of users will inevitably decrease, and revenue will decrease. It is even more absurd to maintain a full dividend. At this time of global economic depression, the interest rates of various enterprises are declining daily, and the company's current operations can still maintain a net profit of more than 6%, which is more than double the interest rate set by national banks in Europe and the United States. Furthermore, the six types of preferred stock of the Shanghai Power Company, with a 6% interest rate, can serve as a precedent. In short, at a time when the social economy is extremely panicked and all industries are in a state of decline, the telephone prices that were set in the past are already considered expensive. We are trying to reduce the burden, so how can we increase it? Our association hopes that your bureau will prioritize the interests of the taxpaying citizens and not only consider the improper gains of a few people, which will incite public anger and lead to other complications. We also hope that you will demand a reduction in usage fees from the telephone company on behalf of the taxpaying citizens in accordance with Section 3 of Article 3 of the contract, and reconsider and cancel the approved price increase proposal to benefit commerce and promote justice. We eagerly await this. Sincerely, to the Public Works Bureau of the Public Concession, the Board of Directors of the French Concession, the First Special District Citizens' Union of Shanghai, the Second Special District Citizens' Union of Shanghai, the Shanghai National Goods Promotion League, the National Goods Factory Union, and the Citizens' National Goods Promotion Association."

Rice Boats Must Detour to Shanghai Due to Dredging of the Wusong River, Fewer Arrivals in the Northern City and Rice Prices Soar Yesterday 179

Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Taihu Lake Water Conservancy Commission is building dams in Beizhuangjing, Yujidun, Caijiazhai, and other places to dredge the Wusong River, resulting in fewer rice boats from the inland arriving in Shanghai and a soaring price increase of 5 jiao. Xin Sheng News Agency reporters have investigated the details as follows:

Building Dams to Dredge the River, The Taihu Lake Water Conservancy Commission is building dams in Yujidun, Caijiazhai, and Beizhuangjing to dredge the Wusong River, and work began yesterday. However, the majority of rice in this city is supplied by Suzhou, Pingwang, Wuxi, Jiangyin, Yixing, Jiashan, Jiaxing, Songjiang, and other places. Except for Jiashan, Jiaxing, and Songjiang, which enter through the South Huangpu, Yujidun is a necessary route for rice boats from other places.

Rice Boats Detour, In normal times, rice boats from Suzhou and Wuxi come to Shanghai via Lujiabang, Sijiangkou, Huangdu, Yujidun, then through the inner Huangpu, Beixinjing, Zhangjiajing, and reach the Wusong River. Since the dam is built in Yujidun, ships must go from Sijiangkou to Baihegang, Qingpu, Songjiang, Minhang, and then detour to the northern city from the outer Huangpu (i.e., the Bund).

Rice Prices Soar, Because rice boats to Shanghai must detour due to the dam construction in Yujidun, only ten ships arrived in the northern city yesterday, twenty fewer than usual. In addition, rice stocks are empty, and rice prices soared by 4 to 5 jiao yesterday. The price of first-grade Changbang rice was 12 yuan and 6 jiao, an increase of 2 jiao, second-grade Xibang rice was 11 yuan and 8 jiao, an increase of 5 jiao, and third-grade Xuanxing rice was 11 yuan and 5 jiao, an increase of 5 jiao. Currently, due to the shortage of goods, prices are expected to remain high.

Another Police Officer Illegally Beats Someone, Wu Fulin Has Been Examined by the Court 180

Following the horrifying case in which the Zhenru police station was found to have caused the death of Zhu Jianqiu, the owner of the Family Food Company, by forcibly injecting water into his nose, resulting in suffocation, and the court sentenced police chief Zhou Pingyuan and police officer Xing Guonong to ten years imprisonment each, another similar case of police brutality resulting in serious injury occurred the day before yesterday. The details are as follows: Wu Fulin, a resident of Dangtu, 45 years old, lives with his wife, Wang, and three children at No. 44 Yongqing West Lane, Roberts Road, Caojiadu. He works as a laborer at the Chengsheng Flower Factory. In 1931, he subleased No. 44, obtaining the qualifications of a second landlord, with a monthly rent of 11 yuan and 3 jiao. According to Wu, because he is illiterate, the rent collector, Mr. Li, successively filled in double rent tickets (two rent tickets per month) for five months. (These rent tickets, because other tenants also discovered double rent tickets and filed lawsuits in the District Court, have been submitted to the court as evidence.) On March 29th, at around 6:00 PM, Mr. Li brought the police to Wu Fulin's house, claiming that Wu was in arrears with his rent. The police arrested Wu and detained him at the Caojiadu police station until 11:00 AM on the 31st, when he was released, but he had already suffered injuries all over his body. Yesterday, Wu's wife, Wu Wang, carried her husband, Wu Fulin, to the prosecutor's office of the District Court, requesting an examination of his injuries. According to Wu Wang, after her husband was arrested by the police on the 29th, she sent food to the station but was refused. Later, after obtaining a business card from a certain prominent person, she was allowed to send food, but her husband had already gone hungry for a day. It was not until around 11:00 AM the day before yesterday (the 31st) that her husband was released, having been detained for two nights and beaten three times. In the last instance, Mr. Li was the first to attack, followed by three police officers who kicked him with wooden sticks or leather shoes, or punched him, even beating him out of the police station, causing injuries that left him unable to move. They also slapped him on both cheeks and struck his ears, even causing deafness. The most severe injuries were to his chest, with bruises all over his legs, indicating serious injuries. After the prosecutor examined him, he was instructed to return home for medical treatment and await further instructions.

Autopsy to Examine Bullets in Last Year's Jin Menggen Murder Case, Wang Xinshan Appeals Death Sentence, Corpse Turns Purplish-Black and Does Not Decompose 181

Jin Menggen, who opened a tea shop in Zhoujiaqiao in western Shanghai, was shot and killed on the morning of April 30th of last year (lunar calendar) at around 5:00 AM while traveling through Hopeland Road. His wives, Jin Bao and Jin Liu, and witnesses testified that the main culprit was Wang Xinshan. After investigation, the District Court sentenced Wang Xinshan to death for premeditated murder. Wang refused to accept the sentence and appealed according to the law. He has been transferred to the Suzhou Higher Court. A hearing was held once, and Wang vehemently proclaimed his innocence. However, it was discovered that there was still a bullet in the deceased's body that had not been extracted at the time. Out of caution, Shao Qinzhi, the criminal judge of the District Court, previously ordered Jin Bao, the deceased's wife, to come to court for questioning last month to ask if she would be willing to have the coffin opened to extract the bullet to examine the bullet's style, which could prove which type of pistol was used. At that time, Jin Bao and others believed that her husband had suffered an unfortunate fate, and they were reluctant to have the coffin opened. The court reasoned that if the coffin was not opened for extraction, how could justice be served, so yesterday it ordered Jin Bao and Jin Liu to carry Jin Menggen's coffin to the Zhenru Forensic Institute to wait for the coffin to be opened. At noon, Judge Shao Qinzhi, along with court clerk and bailiff Zhu Zhiqi, personally visited the Zhenru Forensic Institute and ordered the laborers to open the coffin in accordance with the law. The forensic doctor extracted a bullet from the wound below Jin Menggen's throat and ordered the wives to re-examine the coffin. When the coffin was opened, the wives and concubines of the deceased were extremely distraught and could not help but weep. The corpse did not decompose, but it had turned purplish-black and dry. Because the corpse was wrapped in fabric and placed in a high-quality coffin, it did not easily decompose. Judge Shao Qinzhi asked the family of the deceased a few questions and then returned by car.

Fire on the Wuyang Steamer, Losses Not Significant 182

After the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Wuyang steamer arrived in Shanghai, it was docked at the company's No. 4 pier in Ao Jia Du, Pudong. At around 7:30 PM last night, a burning clump of coal ash suddenly shot out from the steamer's chimney and landed on the canvas of a lifeboat on the deck, immediately igniting a fire. Because no one noticed at the time, the flames spread. The deck was ablaze. A sailor spotted it, immediately rang the bell to raise the alarm, and telegraphed the fire department for assistance. Zhao, the director of the Pudong Fire Department, led his team to the scene in a fire truck to put out the fire. The customs fireboat also arrived shortly after. The fire was extinguished in a short time. One lifeboat, one ventilation window, and approximately one zhang of the platform deck were destroyed.

Investigation of the Robbery at the French Business Water and Electricity Company Not Yet Completed 183

At around 10:00 AM on February 20th of this year, the compradore of the French Business Water and Electricity Company at No. 249 Luban Road, Tu Jinsheng, ordered a cash delivery of 20,000 yuan in silver to be deposited in the bank. Just after he carried it out the door and stepped onto the car, four robbers with guns rushed up and robbed a bag of 4,000 yuan and escaped by car. The French police were notified to investigate. It was not until the evening of the 17th of last month that the French police's Special Bureau's Inspector Jin Jiulin led detectives Zhang Ziying, Qian Yumin, Cai Jinzhang, Zhou Buguang, and patrol detectives to arrest the ringleader and accomplices Yang Yang, Qiu Yanshou, Zhao Zhongheng, Li Zhongxin, Zhu Hanqiang, Pan Yuqing, Liu Shaogen, Zhang Debiao, Fan Youheng, Ren Shaogen, Zhang Yun, Pan Yibang, Zhou Kui, Zhou Lu, Xia Wenfu, Xu Richeng, and Xu Defu, a total of seventeen men and women, at No. 25 Dafang Lane, Fangbang Bridge, No. 34 Derun Lane, Chezhan Road, No. 480 Fangxie Road, and Anshun Lane on Kangti Road and No. 381 Ai Duya Road, New Dafang Hotel, and other places in the Chinese area. Two pistols and sixteen bullets were confiscated and sent to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and investigation. As reported earlier, Judge Sun Peng, along with court clerk Tao Zongkan, came to the First Criminal Court to interrogate them at 10:00 AM yesterday. They first questioned each person's name, age, and origin. Then, according to the police lawyer Yao Zhaodi, because there were many defendants in this case and the case was complicated, the investigation procedures had not yet been completed. He requested an extension of two weeks to investigate the details of the case and file a lawsuit. The court reviewed the report and decided to reschedule the hearing for 10:00 AM on April 10th. The defendants were returned to custody separately. It is rumored that the defendants committed many crimes in the concession, so the police investigation is taking a long time.

National Doctor Cai Songchun and Others Sued for Negligence Causing Injury, Hearing Concluded, Pinellia and Tetrapanax Paper Arise as Main Issue, Expert Opinion Favorable to Defendants 184

Cai Songchun and Cai Bochun, sons of Cai Yousheng, a gynecological expert and national doctor in Jiangwan, are also doctors, practicing medicine on Huaji Road in Hongkou. Recently, they diagnosed Chen Jiang, a woman from Wuxi who was three months pregnant, as having irregular menstruation and used menstruation-inducing drugs such as Pinellia and Tetrapanax Paper, causing her to miscarry. The woman hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Cai Songchun and Bochun in the First Special District Court for negligence causing injury under Article 301 of the Criminal Code. After two hearings, they were instructed to submit an expert opinion from the Shanghai National Doctors Association for further review. As reported earlier, Judge Xiang Yinghua held a continued hearing at the Ninth Criminal Court yesterday afternoon. The two defendants and their lawyer, Lu Qi, also attended. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that the plaintiff's side discovered that both defendants were members of the National Doctors Association and that their father was influential in the association, so their expert opinion would inevitably be biased. Therefore, he requested that the expert opinion be transferred. He did not know if the request had been received and submitted a copy of the "Essentials of Materia Medica" for reference, as the book states that both Pinellia and Tetrapanax Paper are forbidden for pregnant women. Judge Xiang stated that experts should sign individual pledges in accordance with the law, and if there is any perjury, they should be subject to perjury penalties, so the request for transfer should not be considered. The defendant's lawyer, Lu, also presented multiple books of medicine to prove that Pinellia and Tetrapanax Paper can indeed be used for pregnant women. The court then issued the expert opinion, the results of which were favorable to the defendants. After reviewing the opinion, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that the opinion was biased, which was what the plaintiff expected, and requested consideration. Judge Xiang deemed the facts clear and ordered the start of the debate. After the lawyers debated, the court declared the debate concluded and scheduled the sentencing for 2:00 PM next Monday afternoon.

Special District Rickshaw Business Asks to Stop Paying Mutual Aid Fee as Agreed, Eight-Month Period Expired, Yesterday Contacted Public Works Bureau, New Rickshaw Bodies Bulky, Coolies Unwilling to Pull 185

The Public Concession Rickshaw Committee collects a mutual aid fee of 1 yuan and 5 jiao per rickshaw per month. Because the rickshaw business and the Public Works Bureau agreed on August 6th of last year to an eight-month period, which has now expired, and the Public Works Bureau has not yet stopped collecting the fee, the rickshaw business believes that it is unbearable. Therefore, yesterday, a special representative requested the Public Works Bureau to stop collecting the fee in accordance with the agreement. At the same time, after 131 new rickshaws were driven, the coolies still expressed their opposition because the rickshaw bodies were too heavy and difficult to pull. The Rickshaw Committee and the Examination Office convened the coolies together with the rickshaw business representative Gu Songmao to inquire about the situation. As a result, the coolies unanimously stated that they were too heavy and no one was willing to pull them. According to a Xin Sheng News Agency reporter, the Rickshaw Committee believes that the matter is difficult to implement, so it has decided to exchange these new models. The rickshaw business has also designed a new rickshaw and submitted it to the Rickshaw Committee for adoption. As for the mutual aid fee, the rickshaw owners are still continuing to collect it and deposit it in the bank. At the same time, they plan to hold a meeting to negotiate. If the negotiation is ineffective, they will stop paying the fee starting next month.

Trends in Academic Groups and Institutions Since the Republic of China 186

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics on the general situation of domestic academic groups and institutions, which has been reported in the newspapers. The annual increase of domestic academic groups and institutions since the beginning of the Republic of China to the 21st year, as well as a summary of research subjects, are recorded below:

(1) Number of academic groups and institutions: 5 in the first, second, and third years of the Republic of China, 9 in the fourth year, 12 in the fifth and sixth years, 14 in the seventh, eighth, ninth, and tenth years, 18 in the eleventh year, 20 in the twelfth year, 23 in the thirteenth year, 26 in the fourteenth year, 31 in the fifteenth year, 34 in the sixteenth year, 41 in the seventeenth year, 53 in the eighteenth year, 67 in the nineteenth year, 74 in the twentieth year, and 88 in the twenty-first year (including academic institutions: 1 each in the fifth and sixth years of the Republic of China, 2 in the sixth year, 3 each from the seventh to the thirteenth year, 4 in the fourteenth year, 6 in the fifteenth year, 11 in the sixteenth year, 13 in the seventeenth year, 17 in the eighteenth year, 19 in the nineteenth year, 22 in the twentieth year, and 25 in the twenty-first year).

(2) Research subjects: From the first to the third year of the Republic of China, academic groups and institutions researched agricultural science. From the eleventh year, science was added. From the seventeenth year, commerce was added. In terms of each subject: (1) From the eleventh to the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, a total of 47 in science; (2) From the fifth to the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, a total of 34 in agricultural science; (3) From the first to the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, a total of 50 in engineering; (4) From the first to the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, a total of 95 in medicine; (5) From the eleventh to the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, a total of 76 in literature; (6) From the eleventh to the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, a total of 31 in law; (7) From the first to the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, a total of 154 in education; (8) From the seventeenth to the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, a total of 10 in commerce; (9) From the fourth to the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, a total of 82 in general subjects.

Superintendent's Office for Students Studying in Japan Negotiates for Improved Study Abroad Measures 191

(Tokyo Correspondence) Japanese schools have long discriminated against Chinese students, either refusing them admission or establishing special admission procedures for foreigners, indiscriminately accepting Chinese students. The Superintendent's Office for Students Studying in Japan has repeatedly requested improvements from the Japanese authorities regarding this situation, but without result. Zhou Xianwen, the superintendent for students studying in Japan, in view of this, specially hosted prominent figures from the Japanese cultural community at the East Asia Tongwen Society on the 31st of last month. After explaining the current situation of Chinese students studying in Japan in detail, he requested that the following two points be promoted to encourage the Japanese government to realize them as soon as possible: (1) The Japanese side should treat Chinese and Japanese students equally. If some schools do not admit Chinese students, it is not hoped for. If some schools indiscriminately admit Chinese students, they are not welcome. (2) China's various study abroad regulations should be adapted to the Japanese education system, and at the same time, the Japanese side is expected to consider China's legal system in its facilities for Chinese students.

This City Actively Prepares to Celebrate Children's Day; Expanded Preparatory Meeting Held by Various Circles Yesterday Morning; Decided to Hold a Celebration Ceremony on the Morning of the 4th; Children's Film Day Special Invitation to Mayor Wu to Unveil 194

April 4th is the fifth Children's Memorial Day in our country. Children's education groups in this city have already begun preparing for the celebration ceremony. Various situations have been reported in the past. Now, it is learned that the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association held an expanded preparatory meeting of various agencies and groups at the Moonlight Grand Theater yesterday morning to discuss all celebration matters. The details of the meeting are recorded as follows:

Attending Representatives An expanded preparatory meeting of representatives from all walks of life was held at the Moonlight Grand Theater yesterday morning. Lin Kecong and Huang E from the Municipal Party Department, Qian Fugong from the Municipal Education Bureau, Yin Guanzhi from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Chen Lenghui from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, Hu Shuyi from the Children's Welfare Association, Zhu Boyuan from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Jin Zaiye and Cai Yuanzhan from the Public Education Center, Xu Gongmei and Hu Xuguang from the Children's Film Association, Zhou Wanghe from the Children's Morning Post, Chen Tiesheng from the Charity and Childcare Association, Yao Jilang from Wuben Girls' High School, Xu Guanguang from Wanzhu Elementary School, Yu Shumin from Xicheng Elementary School, and more than 30 other people.

Resolutions The meeting was chaired by Bureau Chief Pan,代Hu Shuyi, and recorded by Qian Fugong. The resolutions are as follows: (1) The name of the celebration assembly was determined to be the Shanghai All Circles Celebration of the Fifth Children's Day Memorial Assembly. (2) The time allocation for various mobile activities was stipulated. It was decided that the celebration ceremony would be held at the Moonlight Grand Theater from 9:00 AM to 10:30 AM, the unveiling ceremony for Children's Film Day would be held from 10:30 AM to 12:00 PM, and there would be performances. Children's films would be shown from 1:30 PM to 4:00 PM, and a recreational party would be held at the Municipal Public Education Center from 7:00 PM to 9:00 PM.

Assignment of Responsibilities (3) The assignment of responsibilities was determined. The General Affairs Group was assigned to the Municipal Party Department, Municipal Government, Children's Welfare Association, Charity and Childcare Association, Joint Promotion Association of Student National Products Year, and Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The decoration group was assigned to the Moonlight Grand Theater Children's Film Association and Public Education Center. The Transportation Group was assigned to the Public Security Bureau. The Entertainment Group was assigned to the Municipal Education Bureau, Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and Children's Broadcasting Association. The Reception Group was assigned to the Municipal Party Department and Charity and Childcare Association. The Gifts Group was assigned to the Children's Welfare Association and the Joint Promotion Association of Student National Products Year. The Publicity Group was assigned to the Children's Welfare Association and the Children's Broadcasting Association. The Documentation Group was assigned to the Municipal Party Department.

Transportation of Children (4) Regarding how to arrange transportation for the children attending the meeting, it was decided to limit the transportation to the children from the Benevolence Children's Home, orphanages, and children participating in performances. In addition to the large buses provided by the Municipal Public Security Bureau, one bus each would be borrowed from the Municipal Government and the Municipal Education Bureau, all under the responsibility of the Transportation Group. (5) A letter would be sent to the China General Omnibus Company requesting permission for free bus rides on Children's Day. The resolution was passed. (6) Regarding how to raise funds for the association, it was decided that each agency and group serving on the General Affairs Group would temporarily allocate 20 yuan.

Broadcasting Methods (7) The broadcasting methods were stipulated. It was decided to designate the Shipping Radio Station to broadcast children's programs exclusively from 9:00 AM to 6:00 PM and to send letters to various broadcasting stations in this city requesting them to broadcast children's day programs on that day. (8) A letter would be sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce notifying various businesses to treat children courteously when selling goods on Children's Day. The resolution was passed. (8) A letter would be sent to the Municipal Health Bureau notifying various hospitals to provide free physical examinations and smallpox vaccinations for children on that day. The resolution was passed. The meeting then adjourned.

Mayor Unveils Xu Gongmei, chairman of the Children's Thunder Shadow Committee, sent the following letter to Mayor Wu to request the unveiling: It is hereby noted that our association was declared established on March 26th and that the first committee meeting resolved to cooperate with the Moonlight Grand Theater to hold Children's Film Day at the theater every Tuesday and Friday at 5:00 PM and every Sunday at 10:00 AM, showing films suitable for children's needs and with educational significance for children to watch. It is now scheduled to hold the opening ceremony of Children's Film Day at 9:00 AM on April 4th, Children's Day. At that time, we respectfully request that you, as the esteemed mayor, attend and deliver a speech, so that we may have something to follow.

Releasing a Declaration Shanghai Children's Welfare Association, Children's Film Committee, and Moonlight Grand Theater jointly organized Children's Film Day. They released the following declaration: The 20th century is the century of children. If we don't mind being arbitrary, then we can also say this: the future of film should be the film of children, because only with new children can there be a new country. But if we want to hope for new children, first we must have the tools to create new children. There are naturally many tools to create new children, but we believe that the most effective is film. Future education should be centered on film. The inventor of film, Edison, has already told us this. However, although film is a tool for creating new children, it can also have a bad effect on children. For example, in Europe, films are often the things that create bad teenagers. It is common to see bad teenagers who have escaped from reformatories in movie theaters. Investigating the reasons for their escape, it is actually due to their love of film. Therefore, those who care about education and study the protection of children must have a deep understanding of the issue of children's films. Various countries in Europe and America have special regulations for children to watch films, stipulating the screening time and requiring them to go with their parents. For example, in various cities in Germany, children under the age of six are absolutely not allowed to watch films (as stipulated in Article 2 of the German Film Law). Also, children aged 14 to 18 must be accompanied by their parents to enter the venue. Similarly, the restrictions in England, the United States, Denmark, Sweden, and Italy are also very strict. Needless to say, the reason they are so restrictive is to prevent children's bad behavior. Furthermore, there are two reasons for this. On the one hand, because film is loved by children, they can use their imitative nature in this kind of setting to cultivate their desire for goodness. On the other hand, from a health perspective, for example, in England, films are shown once a week for an hour or more to children aged 14 to 17 to help their development. Our country does not seem to pay much attention to this issue, so there are often cries from babies and shouts from teenagers in movie theaters. This phenomenon is really not appropriate. Human imitation is most developed in childhood. If considerable restrictions are not placed on the viewing of films, then all kinds of bad actions on the film will be imitated one by one without realizing it. Taking Shanghai as an example, although there are more than 40 large and small movie theaters, the films they show are mostly of the love, martial arts, and detective genres, so after children watch them, they unconsciously cultivate theft behavior or lewd thoughts. Some people say that school education in Shanghai has failed to achieve full effect because it has been influenced by bad films. This is really not an overstatement. In view of this, the Children's Welfare Committee has specially invited all parties concerned to organize a Children's Film Committee to study and discuss the film issue. With the consent of the Moonlight Grand Theater, special days have been designated for children to watch films, called Children's Film Day. On these designated days, films that are suitable for children's needs and beneficial to their physical and mental health are shown in order to truly seek some benefits for them. We hope that this will expand from Moonlight to movie theaters throughout the city and even the country, and that there will be such regulations. We dare not say that this alone can create new children for a new China, but there is this tendency and desire.

Municipal Education Association Requests Ministry of Education to Unify Primary and Secondary School Textbooks; Three Principles Decided; Please Submit to the Municipal Education Bureau for Forwarding 195

The Shanghai Municipal Education Association yesterday presented a petition to the Municipal Education Bureau requesting it to forward it to the Ministry of Education to unify textbooks for primary and secondary schools nationwide. The original petition is extracted below: Petition to request the Ministry of Education to unify textbooks for primary and secondary schools nationwide. It is noted that whether school education can produce good results is closely related to the textbooks used. However, since the Revolution, textbooks for various subjects in primary and secondary schools have been used in a mixed manner, with no uniform standard. As a result, School A uses the Commercial Press version, School B uses the Zhonghua version, this year the World version is used, and next year the Kaihu version is used. Even within the same school, the textbooks used for each subject are different, and teachers of the same grade have different choices. The resulting malpractices are that students have uneven levels and have difficulty connecting, and teachers and school authorities also find it difficult to decide due to the complexity of the versions. For this reason, the inability of primary and secondary school education to foresee a revival, although there are many reasons, the lack of uniformity in textbooks is the main crux of the problem. In view of this, the association proposed a discussion at the ninth council meeting, and it was unanimously agreed that the unification of textbooks for primary and secondary schools is a matter of urgent importance. It was decided unanimously to present this petition to your bureau in the name of the association, requesting it to be forwarded to the Ministry of Education. (1) Textbooks should be unified nationwide and edited by the National Compilation and Translation Bureau as soon as possible. (2) Reference books for each subject can be freely compiled and do not need to be restricted. (3) If due to printing reasons, it can be entrusted to a bookstore for joint printing, etc. These principles have been recorded. This matter concerns the teaching efficiency of primary and secondary schools. It should be recorded and presented to your esteemed chief for review, and it is hoped that it will be forwarded to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation, which would be in the public interest.

Great China University Agrees to Reduce Holidays and Shorten the Academic Year; Also Proposes Seven Prerequisites 196

The proposal to shorten the academic year and reduce holidays submitted by Central Committee Member Sun Ke and others to the Fifth Plenary Session of the Central Committee has been resolved by the Central Political Conference. The Ministry of Education has issued an order to various universities to conduct academic research on the matter. Some universities in the north have opposed it, and the reasons have been seen in the newspapers. It is now heard that Great China University in this city has also received the order. President Wang convened a discussion meeting the other day, and Vice President Ou Yuanhuai presented a written opinion, which was modified slightly by Dean of Academic Affairs Lu Jizeng, Dean of the College of Education Tai Shuangqiu, Dean of the College of Arts Wu Zelin, Director of the Teachers College Tong Yinian, Director of the Affiliated Middle School Ni Wenya, Professor Chen Yibai, and others, who contributed their opinions. It was sent to the Ministry on the 28th for reference. In principle, the written opinion generally agrees to the issues of reducing holidays and shortening the academic year, but has several prerequisites attached to the implementation. The full text is tens of thousands of words long. The main points are recorded as follows:

Main Points of Opinion (1) The Issue of Textbook and Time Allocation From the perspective of the curriculum and time allocation of schools at all levels, the length of the academic year is certainly an issue, but a more important issue is how to utilize teaching time. (2) The Issue of the Length of the School System Looking at the current school systems in various countries around the world and the changes in the school system in China over the past 30 years, the length of the school system varies. There is no unified and fixed method. As long as it is needed for the current class environment, there is room for expansion and contraction. (3) The Issue of the Increase or Decrease of Holidays Over the Years The dates of holidays in our country have changed considerably from the founding of the Republic of China to the present. This indicates that there is a lot of room for holiday activity and that there is a tendency to reduce them. (4) The Value of Holidays in Education In theory, holidays have considerable educational value, but in reality, students often fail to utilize holidays or even waste their studies and develop bad habits. (5) The Issue of the Impact of Hot and Cold Weather on Teaching According to the research of Thorndike, if we can encourage students to work hard, then the results of working in hot, humid, stale, and stagnant air are the same as working in ideal conditions. Furthermore, the academic performance of summer schools in the past has been excellent, and there have been no health problems.

Prerequisites (1) Middle School Subjects Are Too Heavy and Class Hours Are Too Long Instead of shortening the academic year, it is better to take the extra time from reducing the holidays and allocate it to supplementary teaching every week to make the student's burden lighter and the content of the course more skilled. (2) Pay Attention to Student Internships and Social Contact Because the holidays are shortened, students have fewer opportunities to contact society. The school should stipulate a certain amount of time each semester and incorporate student internships to prevent them from becoming isolated from society. (3) The government should pay attention to the issue of graduates' career prospects Because the academic year is shortened, there will be more graduates each year, and the issue of career prospects will naturally be more difficult to resolve. (4) The administrative management equipment and the age of admission for schools at all levels must be re-standardized in order to achieve sound and reasonable operation. For teachers, salaries should be increased, seniority-based pay increases and retirement benefits should be implemented, and the number of teachers should be increased to allow them to take turns taking one day off a week, or several months off every one or two years to continue their studies. If the two departments of high school and middle school are changed to a semester system, this would be easier to do. (9) More room for flexibility should be left to local areas. The best way to handle winter and summer holidays is to stipulate that a few days off will be granted when the temperature and humidity reach a certain degree, otherwise no holidays will be granted. (6) As for the implementation steps, it is best to have the Ministry of Education designate a few universities, middle schools, and elementary schools in the north and south to conduct trials first. If the results of the trials are indeed successful, then expand it to general schools. (7) It is also a way to shorten the academic year by acknowledging the credits of night schools and summer schools. It is heard that Ou Yuanhuai's written opinion will be published in the May issue of the Education Magazine to seek advice from colleagues in the education community.

Shen Bao Extracurricular School Opens a Day School: Decides to Open English and Arithmetic Classes; Classes Officially Start on April 10th 200

The Shen Bao Extracurricular School attached to this newspaper, in response to requests from all walks of life, has decided to trial run a day school this semester. Enrollment has been open for many days, but due to insufficient numbers, it has been decided to open English and Arithmetic classes. Classes will officially start on April 10th. A notice has been sent to the registered students as follows: Dear Sir/Madam, Our school has been trial running a day class this semester. Enrollment has been open for a long time, but all classes have not been fully enrolled. However, time waits for no one, and the summer vacation will soon be here, so we must urgently seek to open the school. Therefore, we convened all the registered students to the school for a discussion on March 30th and decided that "the English and Arithmetic classes will be opened first this semester (the other classes will not be opened). From April 10th to July 10th, the English class will be held from 1:00 PM to 2:20 PM, and the Arithmetic class will be held from 2:40 PM to 4:00 PM (a total of three full months and thirteen weeks, with classes held six days a week from Monday to Saturday, and each subject taught for 80 minutes each day, which is equivalent to 125 hours in ordinary schools). As for the teaching methods, the English class will have the teacher select a Chinese article each day and translate it into English in the classroom in a discussion format. It is hoped that in this short period of time, all the points that should be paid attention to when writing in English can be raised step by step. This teaching method is expected to be of great help to high school students. In addition to teaching algebra in an orderly manner from simultaneous linear equations, the Arithmetic class will also assign a book of geometry and trigonometry each as extracurricular reading, and set aside 30 minutes each day in class to study them." It is sent to you by special letter. Those who wish to join, please come to the school to pay the fees within the three days of April 2nd, 3rd, and 4th (14.5 yuan for one subject, 28.5 yuan for two subjects, and the previously paid registration fee can be used to offset the tuition). If you do not wish to join, please come to the school within the above three days to collect your registration fee in order to close the matter.

Ministry of Education Orders Adoption by Junior High School Physical Education Teachers: Detailed Syllabus for Junior High School Physical Education Instruction 210

In order to provide appropriate teaching materials for physical education teachers in primary and secondary schools nationwide, the Ministry of Education has specially commissioned physical education experts to write "Detailed Syllabus for Physical Education Instruction for Junior High School Boys I," "Detailed Syllabus for Physical Education Instruction for Junior High School Girls," "Detailed Syllabus for Physical Education Instruction for Senior High School Boys," "Detailed Syllabus for Physical Education Instruction for Senior High School Girls," and "Detailed Syllabus for Physical Education Instruction for Primary Schools." The "Detailed Syllabus for Physical Education Instruction for Junior High School Boys" edited by Wu Yunrui, totaling three volumes, with each volume applicable to one grade level, has now been ordered by the Ministry of Education for unified adoption by physical education teachers in junior high schools nationwide. The first volume, for use in the first year of junior high school, comprises 30% games teaching materials, 16% ball games teaching materials, 20% track and field teaching materials, and 27% apparatus exercises teaching materials. It is divided into two semesters, each lasting twenty weeks, with excellent teaching organization and innovative teaching materials. The second volume is for use in the second academic year, with a slight decrease in games and ball games teaching materials compared to the first year, and a slight increase in track and field and apparatus exercises. The entire book is divided into two semesters, each lasting twenty weeks, with unlimited applications of teaching materials. The third volume is for use in the third academic year, adding self-defense activities and swimming teaching materials in addition to games, ball games, track and field, and apparatus exercises. The arrangement of various sports is differentiated according to different seasons. The entire book is divided into two semesters, each lasting twenty weeks. The entire three-volume set has a retail price of 2 yuan and 25 cents, plus 14 cents for registered mail, and is distributed by the Qinfen Bookstore at 392 Rue du Père Robert, Shanghai.

Preparation for the Shanghai International Sports Association 211

Mr. Bausi Zenggaodi, a Westerner from the Philippines with a passion for sports, has initiated the organization of the Shanghai International Sports Association to promote peak impact sports. He has invited renowned professors to provide guidance, aiming to promote participation. The entrance fee is extremely reasonable. The venue is currently being sought. The association's charter is recorded below.

Shanghai International Sports Association Charter: Purpose (1) To enhance friendship among people from all walks of life in society; (2) To promote sports, exercise members' physical and mental strength; (3) To improve various sports; (4) To organize various teams and directly train athletes representing the association in various public competitions. Special training courses: (1) Western boxing; (2) Western wrestling and Japanese Judo; (3) Physical exercise (including weightlifting and muscle development); (4) Weight gain and loss (including diet and exercise materials); (5) Indoor sports and calisthenics (including parallel bars, high bars, iron rings, somersaults, diving, and stacking gymnastics, etc.); (6) Lectures, indoor games, etc. Membership qualifications and categories: Any person, regardless of gender, may become a member of the association. There are two types of members: ordinary members and special members. (1) Ordinary members may enjoy the right to use all facilities and gyms of the association at any time during the membership period, and may participate in special training classes held every week. (3) Ordinary members and special members may bring relatives and friends to the association's gym and clubhouse, but non-members of the association may not enjoy various rights. Membership fees: (1) Ordinary members (male): 4 yuan for the joining fee, and 3 yuan for the monthly membership fee thereafter; (2) Ordinary members (female): 3 yuan for the joining fee, and 2 yuan for the monthly membership fee thereafter; (3) Special members (male): 4 yuan for the joining fee, and 3 yuan per month thereafter. Those who join special training classes will pay an additional 3 yuan per month; (4) Special members (female): 3 yuan for the joining fee, and 2 yuan per month thereafter. Those who join special training courses will pay an additional 2 yuan per month. Clubhouses and other gyms: The association's clubhouse and gym are open from 9:00 AM to 9:00 PM daily. The clubhouse is equipped with books, magazines, board games, a dining room, and other facilities to provide members with the same comfort as they would find in their homes. The gym is equipped with the following equipment: barbells, parallel bars, high bars, weightlifting racks, dumbbells, clubs, sandbags, boxing gloves, wrestling mats, wooden horses, rowing machines, calisthenics equipment, jump ropes, stretching balls, massagers, punching bags, towels, and shower rooms. Other equipment will be added at any time as deemed necessary by the board of directors. Staff members may use the various facilities of the association and the gym during designated hours. Teachers: Each course of the association is taught by renowned teachers and championship athletes. (A) Professor Gaudiso, Bachelor of Mechanical Engineering from the University of the Philippines and sports expert in the Philippine heavy impact championship, teaches the following courses: (1) Western boxing; (2) Physical fitness training; (3) Indoor calisthenics and flexibility exercises; (4) Weight gain and loss. (B) Professor Salamendo, former Chinese light impact competition champion, teaches various boxing competitions and teams. Boxing competitions will be held once a month, with prizes awarded by the association to the winners. Wrestling competitions, weightlifting, and other indoor sports competitions will be scheduled by the board of directors at any time. Various teams may be organized by members of the association and may participate in various public competitions. The association also holds tea parties and banquets, which are organized by the board of directors.

County People's Education Hall Holds Children's Air Rifle Target Shooting Competition Children's Day at the Hall's Sports Ground 212

The Shanghai County Minhang Public Education Hall, in order to instill military knowledge in children, promote martial spirit, and awaken society's attention to physical education, organized a children's air rifle target shooting competition, hosted by the hall's director, Jin Zuobin, and physical education instructor, Cheng Ji'an. The competition was held at the hall's sports ground on Children's Day afternoon at 2:00 PM. The age of participants ranged from seven to fifteen years old. The competition events were divided into three distances: 10 meters, 15 meters, and 20 meters. The competition groups were divided into Group A (12 to 15 years old) and Group B (7 to 11 years old). In the 10-meter preliminary round, each person fired three shots, and those who hit two shots had the right to participate in the semi-finals. In the 15-meter semi-finals, each person fired three shots, and those who hit one shot had the right to participate in the finals. In the 20-meter finals, each competitor could fire five shots, and the four competitors with the most hits would be selected according to their scores. The target was a round circle with a diameter of two feet and five inches, divided into categories A, B, and C, with two lines. Hitting category A earned 200 points, category B earned 150 points, and category C earned 100 points. The air rifles and bullets used in the competition were provided by the hall. The top four winners in each group received prizes.
