Tidbits 214

— (Zhou Tingfang)

Wine is indeed a valuable medicine at times, but it can also be a potent temptation. The great English playwright Shakespeare has a few wonderful lines cursing wine: "O that men should put an enemy in their mouths to steal away their brains! that we should, with joy, pleasance, revel, and applause, transform ourselves into beasts!"

However, the harm of wine is only the more obvious kind. Other things like opium and red pills are even more like "putting an enemy in their mouths," as Shakespeare said. Linghu Zhao

Himalayan Expedition 215

— Dan Yun

The benefits of exploration are infinite. Christopher Columbus was able to discover the New World because he had the spirit of exploration. This is the best example. Conservatism can often lead to the decline of a nation, while risky advancement can make a nation prosper. European and American nations are the most adventurous and progressive, and it can be seen that the strength of their countries is not without reason.

Everyone knows that Mount Everest in the Himalayas is the highest peak in the world, about 29,141 feet high. It is covered with snow all year round, and the cold is bone-chilling. It is a place where living things cannot live. Cowardly people would never dare to go up and explore, but European and American explorers have a kind of stubbornness to do something that they clearly know they cannot do, and often want to explore the Himalayas. There have been several expeditions to the Himalayas so far, but each time, in addition to sacrificing several lives, no concrete results have been obtained.

Recently, I heard that another "1935 French Himalayan Mountaineering Team" led by Mr. Aisijiala will explore from this year. Don't they care about the lessons of the past? Don't they cherish their precious lives? No, they dare to do this great act because they are driven by the spirit of risky advancement. This spirit is very worthy of our admiration.

Russian Ah Da 216

— Rong Yu

Whenever I come to Shanghai from home and walk through Baoshan Road, which has been ravaged by war and become desolate and remote, I always encounter such a fellow: wearing an old and dirty Western suit, because there is no lining shirt inside, the rough and hairy muscles seem to be about to emerge from the cracks and holes. His cheeks are full of yellow and stiff beards, reflecting his rolling blue eyes, which are so frightening. When he sees someone passing by, he first gives you a salute, and then says in imperfect Chinese, "Sir, one copper, thank you!" This fellow is Luo Zhu Ah Da, whom everyone in Shanghai knows, also known as Russian Loafer. I am not a passive philanthropist like a Buddhist grandmother, and I am usually unwilling to give alms to beggars; only when I see this foreign exile, I cannot help but give him a little, so he recognizes me as his old customer. Every time he sees me, he puts on a smiling face, salutes, and waits quietly for my copper coin to be thrown into his tattered felt hat.

One day, I ran into him again, but I happened to have no copper coins with me, so I took out a small silver dollar and gave it to him, and told him, "I won't give you any more this month." He nodded, and indeed for several weeks, he never stretched out his hand when he saw me passing by.

One evening, I walked through Baziqiao. There are many houses there that were destroyed by artillery fire and have not been rebuilt. Some lead sheets are supported on the broken walls and ruins, which have become the comfortable nest of the beggars. I saw that Luo Song Ah Da was also sitting high inside, taking out the harvest he had gained during the day, ordering the little beggar to buy shochu and side dishes, as if he was treating guests. And many Chinese beggars also took out cigarette butts and asked him to smoke, with a friendly attitude, which also eliminated racial and national prejudices!

Famous Painter Wang Luchun Passed Away at the Age of Sixty-Six. Did His Love of Meat Confirm a Common Saying? As an Old Friend, I Cannot Help But Offer a Poem 217

— Tian Xu Wo Sheng

Bitterly recall old Wang's bibulous friend. How has his drinking been recently? Who knew that after one parting three years ago, he would be separated from the mortal world forever.

Half an acre of garden is desolate, and old wishes are empty. The world is vast, and I feel separated from my home. I can't forget drinking in the building outside the embrace. The last time we tasted sweet and sour fish together. (At the West Lake Exposition, we drank together on the lake. Luchun had jaundice and did not eat fish. I said, "Are you afraid of death? I think we are immortal and can endure suffering." Luchun understood and ate two more fish.)

His lacquer script is more wonderful than Jin Dongsou. His pastel copies are better than Yun Shouping. He owes me thirty years of poetic and drinking debts, which are now all unpaid.

Cai Yi has a daughter who can pass on his legacy. Deng Bo has no son and can only listen to fate. I say that life is originally a dream. Why distinguish between chickens, dogs, and immortals? (Luchun has no son but has a daughter named Ziyue, who is named Jin Guan. Now the obituary has a grandson, who is probably the son of the daughter. The system of clan peaches is no longer valued in this era, but the meaning of loving relatives is not extinguished. This is one breath of our nation's survival. Those who do not regard each other as Qin and Yue all rely on this.)

Little Western Sky 218

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 11: Night Talk of a Sad Life, Originally a Dream, Footprints Scattered, Wind and Rain Too Deceptive

Jia Duocai listened to her words and was also dazed. At this time, he recovered his consciousness after drinking tea. The kerosene lamp on the table was probably set with a short wick and could not fully absorb the oil, so the flame was not very bright, and the shadows of people were somewhat blurred. Especially the tragic sound of the wind was blowing outside the wall again, which added to the unhappiness in people's hearts. He was silent, and Yang Huanhua was even more silent. After Jia Duocai finished drinking the cup of tea, Huanhua said to him: "Mr. Jia, think about it, what kind of life am I living? Thinking about the fate of others, how dare I live this life down? I dare not say the word 'marry someone.' If anyone goes south and is short of people to serve, I can serve him to Jiangnan. When I get to Jiangnan, I don't want anyone to pay my wages. I am willing to go home myself." Jia Duocai felt that the conditions she said were so low that it made her even more pitiful. So he said to her: "The opportunity you are talking about is not so difficult. I will pay attention to it with you." Huanhua said: "I also know very well that people like me are not worthy of Mr. Jia's eyes. She said to herself, and her face turned red. Jia Duocai scratched his head and smiled. You are too polite. Think about it, we can't take advantage of people in danger. Fortunately... fortunately, we..." He really couldn't find a suitable sentence to continue, so he just scratched his head. Yang Huanhua tightened her face and interjected: "I am not such a confused person. I am embarrassed to say this. I know that Mr. Jia likes the girl from Gansu very much. I have nothing to curry favor with you, so I will rent you as a ready-made matchmaker tomorrow. Originally, only women can know women's thoughts. If I say a few words according to what is in their hearts, it may be easier to succeed. There is nothing else to say. After drinking your wedding wine in the future, I will serve your new wife back to the south." (271)

Royal Fragrance, Misty Records 219

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

As for the colors dyed on the silk, they were worth boasting about by the Empress Dowager! She not only used all the various colors in the world, but also divided each color into dozens of shades, from dark to light. For example, the color "green" was dyed into dark green in the first twist, and then gradually faded, from grass green, tender green, lake green, to the lightest; this lightest twist was already as pale as white. This project seemed to be not very difficult, but in reality it was extremely difficult. The girls used all their energy to do it. However, when they were dried, dozens or hundreds of colors gathered together, and when they were illuminated by the bright sunlight, they were extremely beautiful. If you look at them for a while, your eyes will surely be dizzy!

I still remember very clearly the first time I followed the Empress Dowager to visit.

As usual, dozens of dyed silks were drying in the stone square. The Empress Dowager first looked at them roughly, and then walked to a pole of blue silk, starting from the deepest twist and carefully looking at it gradually. At this time, the girls were already kneeling on the ground, waiting silently for the old lady to speak. Because she often criticized them for how the dyeing was not good, how the drying was not good; or she would also express her own opinions on improving the dyeing method. Of course, the opinions she expressed verbally were as irresistible as the written imperial edict; although dyeing silk was a small matter, in the eyes of these silk-making craftsmen, it was a matter of great importance. (282)

A Record of a Commander 220

— You Ming

Massage therapy is especially prominent with one-finger Zen, and its effectiveness sometimes surpasses that of medicine. As far as I know, there is a one-finger Zen massage doctor named Huang Yizhao on South Chengdu Road in Shanghai. He is the son of the famous doctor Huang Hanru. He has a profound family knowledge and is good at treating stubborn diseases. He has a very precise understanding of pulse principles and deeply researches the source of diseases, so his treatment has many miraculous effects. The daughter of Mr. Wang Xifan, the younger cousin of the former Minister of Foreign Affairs, Dr. Wang Zhengting, was physically weak. Last winter, she suddenly suffered from scrofula under her right ribs. At the beginning, she was treated with medicine by doctors, but it gradually grew larger in a few days, and the area became harder. She could not turn her neck and had chills and fever. Later, through the introduction of his friend Mr. Zongxun, Mr. Huang was invited to treat her. The chills and fever completely subsided in two or three days, and her neck moved as usual in ten days, and the affected area was more than half smaller. In about three weeks, she had fully recovered. The author Huang and his son have written Huang's Medical Talks. I have always had a copy, which describes in detail the functions of one-finger Zen massage. Reading his book, I know that the medical skills of Huang and his son have an incredible mystery.

Goldfish Ramblings 221

— Wu Jiren

Last Saturday afternoon, Mr. Zheng Xiaoqiu suddenly became happy and invited me to take a trip to Zhabei. We took his car to the area of Song Park Road and Zhijiang Temple. Mr. Zhu Chun, of Liuchun Goldfish Garden, had just returned to Wuxi, so we missed him. However, we did meet Mr. He, who lives in the garden and is extremely fascinated by goldfish. No matter how well he raises fish at home, the air and sunlight are ultimately not as good as at Liuchun Garden. He and Mr. Zhuang share the same interests. Coincidentally, the landlord was building a new house, so he moved here to be with thousands of ornamental fish morning and evening, laughing and chatting among them. I know his heart must be very happy, perhaps even more than being a ruler in the south.

Mr. He guided us around Liuchun Garden once. The scale and facilities are the best in Shanghai. Xiaoqiu chose to buy four "Looking to the Sky" goldfish and four calico goldfish, satisfied with the prices. Then we went to the Ma family's fish farm. The owner is from the north and his breeding of ball goldfish and coarser breeds is quite remarkable. However, he does not pay much attention to delicate breeds like pearlscales, bubble eyes, and upturned gills. The climate and customs of the north and south are different, and the water and soil also affect the nature of the fish. Therefore, fish breeders have each developed their own specialties. Less than a hundred steps from the Ma family's farm is a fish garden run by the martial arts star Mr. Zha Ruilong himself. The facilities are quite good, but unfortunately, he used his staff poorly, and it is in a state of disrepair. Even the fish are not many anymore. I heard that Mr. Zha sacrificed thousands of gold coins.

On the way back. After walking less than three hundred steps, Mr. He pointed out a new fish garden that was under construction, with digging the ground to make ponds and turning the soil to install tanks. In less than two months, we will be able to see many lively fish chasing each other among the green algae.

At the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Wharf, where we were seeing off Zhou Hu as he went abroad, I met the owner of the "Violet" and we talked about goldfish. He told me that in the first month of this year, several five- or six-year-old violet orchid goldfish developed frostbite (see note below) due to the long period of rainy weather. He displayed them in a washbasin, exposing them to sunlight. One day, he was careless and the neighbor's cat stole and devoured them. Such five- or six-year-old violet orchid goldfish are rare even in Suzhou, not to mention elsewhere. The owner must be very upset.

I haven't seen Mr. Zhang Mengzhou for almost half a year, and I haven't visited his Lin She Fish Garden on Xietu Road for a long time. Xiaoqiu suggested we visit, so we drove there. The bamboo fence was neatly arranged and the new house was completed. The three rooms facing south were bright and clean. The tanks and ponds were planned in an orderly manner. Compared to the humble beginnings of the past year, it was like two completely different places. I recall when I was establishing the Fish Paradise, I ran around for several months and managed things, but in the end, due to disagreements, I let Mr. So-and-so take over. Therefore, Mr. Zhang's hard work can be imagined. If fish had consciousness, they would surely multiply new breeds to dance for Mr. Zhang! I laugh.

My younger brother, Baozhi, has also recently developed a fondness for fish. He has installed more than twenty tanks in the courtyard. He has collected about ten species. In addition to a gardener changing the water, he does the feeding himself every morning. Last summer, nearly ten thousand small fish hatched. Unfortunately, there was a drought, and the well water was scarce. As a result, it was very difficult to get water, and the fish died one after another. When the rain finally came, the few remaining small fish did not grow very large. When I visited home at the end of the year, I saw breeds such as upturned gills, jade tiger heads, etc., which were still quite impressive.

(Note) Frostbite is when the fish's body develops small white spots, including the gills. In severe cases, it turns into white patches. The cause of the disease is prolonged cloudy days with little sunlight. The cure is to expose the fish to strong sunlight. Mr. Dong Tianya, the set design director of the Star Film Company, used scientific treatment two years ago, using five thousand candlepower electric lights to irradiate the fish, and the fish were cured. However, be extra careful when irradiating, and pay special attention to the water temperature.

Results of September Cotton Yarn Grade Appraisal: 10-Count Coarse Yarn Downgraded by 4 Yuan; Special Margin Increased by 3 Yuan for New April Cotton Transactions 228

The Chinese Cotton Yarn and Cloth Exchange convened a cotton yarn grade appraisal meeting on March 25th to review the grades of cotton yarn for the September 1935 delivery period as a substitute for delivery. The result of the grade review was that the grade of 16-count cotton yarn was unchanged and the rise and fall was the same as in August. The grade of 20-count cotton yarn was only changed by reducing the grade of the English Yangshupu Factory's Shepherd Yarn by 5 yuan in August and now changed to 6 yuan. The remaining 20-count yarns were unchanged, but all 10-count yarns were downgraded by 4 yuan compared to the August grade. The reason for this was that the price of Indian cotton velvet flowers used to make the 10-count yarns was low, and the factories could make a profit from spinning, so the exchange was afraid that the low price would affect the market price of speculative selling. The grades of 10-count coarse yarns were therefore greatly reduced in order to regulate them. The revised procedures and grade prices are listed below for reference:

Yesterday's flour market was stable in the morning. Foreign wheat was quoted at approximately 0.20 yuan higher in Chicago, and Canadian wheat was approximately 0.04 yuan higher. Sellers did not dare to substantially reduce their offers, while buyers still showed greed. As a result, the opening prices for all months were approximately 0.01 or 0.02 yuan higher. However, as settlement had just passed, actual sales were cautious and stagnant. Although the situation was stable, trading was not very active. When the afternoon session opened, it was initially stable, with the current month continuing to be 0.075 yuan higher. Later in the session, prices showed weakness because manufacturers were slightly short-selling far-term contracts, and near-term customers were also inactive. However, the current stocks of flour at various mills were not yet plentiful, so there was little hope for an oversupply in the short term. As a result, the current month closed 0.01125 yuan higher, May closed 0.005 yuan higher, June closed 0.01125 yuan higher, July closed 0.00075 yuan lower, August closed 0.005 yuan higher, and the opening price for September was 0.36 yuan, with no changes at the close.

Yesterday's wheat market showed a trend of near-term firmness and far-term stability. Foreign wheat quotations were favorable, and the current month's opening price was increased by 0.07 yuan compared to the end of the previous month because the supply of old stock was scarce and market inventories were not plentiful, which caused investors in the industry to gradually think about raising prices. However, trading was very light afterwards, and there were no new entries or exits. For far-term months, investor sentiment was slightly weaker due to the fine weather, but later, buyers surged in, bringing a slightly firm trend. Looking ahead, the key to future price movements will be whether the new wheat crops are in good condition. As a result, the current month closed 0.07 yuan higher, August closed 0.01 yuan higher, and the remaining months were unchanged. In the current wheat market, due to the scarcity of arrivals, customers were bargaining prices up, and various offers were increased by 0.02 or 0.03 yuan. (North Shanghai) Yesterday, the Yujidun Riverway was still passable, resulting in approximately 30 ships arriving from various locations. White Yuan rice sales were brisk, and retail sales gradually faded, with prices increasing by nearly 0.10 yuan. The remaining goods showed a slightly tight trend.

(Foreign Rice) Yesterday, foreign rice sales were active due to continuous purchases from local customers, which stirred investor sentiment, and buyers were particularly persistent. Yesterday, local and Chongsha, Jiaojiao, and Shaoxing groups competed to purchase over 2,000 bags of Kexian rice, and prices also increased by 0.10 yuan. Keyuan rice was affected by foreign Yuan rice, and the market was flat. Yesterday, 1,000 bags of Shashi Jiyuan rice were sold from this street at a price of only 9.06 yuan.

Free Talk

Other Scholars 231

— Another Realm

Mo Di coined a nickname for the scholar-official class of the time, calling them "Other Scholars". "Other Scholars" was in contrast to his self-proclaimed "Inclusive Scholars." He explained the difference between inclusiveness and otherness, saying:

"Those who follow the will of Heaven are inclusive; those who oppose the will of Heaven are other. Inclusiveness takes righteousness as its way; otherness takes force as its way."

But what is following Heaven, and what is opposing Heaven? He did not explain this. It seems that ancient people always liked to talk about "the will of Heaven," as if the will of Heaven was like this, and there was nothing more to say! But this easily leads to fatalism. Mo Di was not a fatalist; his saying that following Heaven naturally meant taking righteousness as the way, while taking force as the way was opposing Heaven. From this, we can see that Mo Di did not blindly support the established facts. If these established facts came from force, he would still "differ" from them.

But here is a problem: if we analyze the facts before us, we can clearly see whether they are righteous or not; but if they are not what we have witnessed with our own eyes, but matters in the hands of the previous generation or the generation before that, or even matters from hundreds or thousands of years ago, how can we discern whether they are righteous or not? The fact tells us that the so-called history of today is often not a history of righteousness, and the history of righteousness is often erased by later historians. Why? Because the history of righteousness is often mostly unfavorable to the established facts. After the historians twist it with their pens, it seems that those who use force are "following the will of Heaven," while those who are righteous become "opposing the will of Heaven." Later generations do not investigate and often confuse black and white, and we cannot distinguish who is an inclusive scholar and who is an other scholar.

Therefore, when we read history now, we cannot rely solely on these materials that praise force, and we cannot ignore those unofficial histories, notes, and novels. "Digging up" other sources is also a valuable resource.

Curiosities Picked Up 232

— Wopu

(1) Feng Yulan

In Zang Jinsu's Yuan Qu Selection of One Hundred Plays, except for Six Types: Children's Reunion, Jin Anshou's Outskirts of the City, Willow Mistakenly Enters the Peach Garden, Opposite Jade Comb, Xiao Shulan. These are actually works of the early Ming Dynasty, which have long been verified. According to Dong Ji's General Catalogue Summary of Musical Dramas, Volume 4, the entry on Feng Yulan states:

"According to the play, there is Qingjiangpu, which was opened by Chen Xuan, the Earl of Pingjiang, in the tenth year of Yongle in the Ming Dynasty. It also says that Vice Censor-in-Chief Jin Gui is the Pacification Commissioner of Tingnan. "Vice Censor-in-Chief" and "Pacification Commissioner" are both official titles of the Ming Dynasty. This was likely written by someone after the Yong and Xuan periods, and falsely attributed to a Yuan Dynasty person."

These two pieces of evidence are very strong. Although it is said that the spoken parts in the Yuan Qu Selection are mostly not from the Yuan Dynasty and are suspected of being added later, we have no reason to prove that they have ever been tampered with. Therefore, this last type of variety play in the Qu Selection, Feng Yulan's Crying Jiang Zhou by Moonlight, must be considered a work of the Ming Dynasty, reducing the total number of Yuan Dynasty musical dramas that have been passed down. In addition to Feng Yulan, there are also twenty-two anonymous works in the Yuan Qu Selection. Perhaps there are also works of the Ming Dynasty similar to this that have not been identified, which is not known at this time?

(2) The Story of the Tavern

The story of Wang Zhihuan writing on the wall of a tavern does not seem to have attracted the attention of playwrights in the Yuan and early Ming dynasties. It was not until the late Ming and early Qing dynasties that it became a popular theme for playwrights. According to what is currently known to be recorded, there are variety plays: Zhang Longwen's Tavern Swallow, Qiu Lian's Tavern (Early Collection of Qing Dynasty Variety Plays) and musical dramas: Zheng Zhiwen, Lu Jianzeng and Jin Jiao (?) all three named The Story of the Tavern. Zheng Zhiwen's version is very rare. Zheng Xidi has a collection (see Gou Ji's New Losses and New Discoveries of Chinese Opera History Materials). The Lu and Jin versions have quite a few problems that are worth studying. The Story of the Tavern, which is not difficult to obtain now, is about a singing girl named Xie Bianfa, and it is uncertain whether it belongs to Lu? or Jin? There is no fixed conclusion. Jin Jiao's version may not even have existed. This version of The Story of the Tavern has a preface by the Shandong Cangfu of Qianlong Yimao (1759). The preface states:

"Yangzhou is the most prosperous place in the world, and the bamboo flute" singing of "Zhuxi" has been盛 from the Tang Dynasty to the present. It is fitting that there are many actors in various departments. However, people are tired of the old, and if a new script is heard, they will rush to buy and perform it, in order to change the current situation of those who are writing, most of whom are motivated by profit. Those who guide depravity are dissolute and forget to return, and those who describe the strange are absurd and outrageous. Stupid men, foolish women, and young children praise them, which will lead to harm to people's hearts and customs. I am very disapproving of this, but I have nothing to replace it. Lan Jing born in Quanjiao, is keen on elegance and literary pursuits. He asked me for poems after traveling to Daoyou. When the poems were completed, he mentioned the story of writing on the wall in the tavern recorded in the Tang Dynasty Strange Records. He said that since ancient times, many loyal and brave deeds have been omitted from official history but included in story collections. They can all be set to music in musical dramas. "Shuangyi" is adorable and can add luster to our party. If it is set to music, it should not lose its elegance. It is a pity that the poets since the Yuan and Ming dynasties have not done so. Lan Jing said yes, then traveled to Yangzhou after a year and presented me with the complete Story of the Tavern. I loved its clear and elegant lyrics but was troubled by its complex plot. When I arranged it according to the musical scale, there were also some parts that were not completely in harmony. So I discussed it with Xiyuan, and we consulted with veteran theater instructors to arrange the stage, slightly changing its mechanism so that it was suitable for both popular and elegant tastes. I occasionally indulged in drunken writing, expressing my thoughts freely. Although I was not familiar with musical notation, my intention followed my pen, and it naturally matched the beat. There were also things that I could not explain. After the Story was completed, Shen Changzhou happened to arrive and played the final song. Mr. Shen praised it and said: It is a good medicine for the two families who guide depravity and describe the strange. He wrote six quatrains on the book and advised it to be printed."

Shen Guiyu's six inscription poems are also still there. There is also a postscript by Ningdu Lu Duanchen. This preface is a very important record, which can be used to explain the difference between the Lu and Jin versions. We know that Lu Jianzeng was the salt transport commissioner of Lianghuai, stationed in Yangzhou, and a native of Dezhou. Therefore, this Shandong Cangfu is undoubtedly his pseudonym. The original author of the extant musical drama, Quanjiao Lan Jing, was probably his client. Because he consulted and revised it (judging from the tone in the preface, it could even be said that he rewrote or even collaborated on it), and he entrusted it to printing, and there was no official name of the author on the book, later it was considered to be his work, and it was listed together with Yu Chichi Tower. It is feared that Yu Chichi Tower was also not Lu's own work, but was penned by Zhu Gongfang (Ben), as seen in the Qiu Deng Conghua, cited in Jiang Ruizao's Novel Research. Lu was in charge of elegance in the southeast at the time and reviewed (or, to put it bluntly, seized) several songs, and it was common for literati to become patrons of opera writers. Shen's inscription poem even says, "Official pavilion filling lyrics, the rhyme is the clearest." For generations, this musical drama has been regarded as Lu's work, which is not necessarily wrong. But the jokes that have been passed down are obviously based on the misunderstanding that Quanjiao Lan Jing is the same as Ling Jiao, whose courtesy name is Lanjiao. One word error has led to the addition of a Jin version of The Story of the Tavern. Since Li Diaoyuan's Yucun Opera Talk, Wang Guowei's Opera Records, and Wu Mei's General Theory of Chinese Opera, the writings on opera have mostly inherited this error, and no one has corrected it. Could it be that Wang and Wu have not seen this version of The Story of the Tavern?

On the Shanghai China Bookstore's fourteenth volume of new and old books, there is A Thin Story of the Tavern in two volumes, written and printed during the Qianlong period, signed by Quanjiao Wu _, which is probably the same version as the one mentioned above and not another version. But the several copies of A Thin Story of the Tavern that I have seen all do not involve the words "Wu _". I wonder what the bookstore is basing its claim on? Or perhaps it is simply registered here because the local tribute scholars from Quanjiao are similar, and the courtesy name of Lanjiao is similar. However, Zun Sheng was born in 1755 (Qianlong Bingzi), and when Shandong Cangfu and Lan Jing's Story of the Tavern were written, he was only five years old. Shen Guiyu, who wrote the inscription poem, died in 1779 (Qianlong Jichou), and Wu was only fifteen years old. It seems impossible for him to have written the book! Unless there is really another Story of the Tavern, and this book is not the same version, then there is no contradiction in time. (To be continued)

Deep Alley 233

— Zhou Erfu

Heavy steps,

Dragging a tired, thin shadow,

In the deep alley,

In the quiet deep alley,

Step by step…

With the mood of a wanderer,

From endless darkness,

To endless darkness.

Little Foot Beans 234

— Qinwen

Little foot beans are also called gizzard beans because they are oval in shape, with many wrinkles along the bean tip, like a chicken gizzard. They are made from a type of edamame; salt is added during cooking, so the light greenish-blue skin is covered with white salt. Chewing them is chewy and firm, with a salty and savory taste and a fragrant aroma. They are called little foot beans because they are wrapped in Fuyang straw paper, in pointed packages, as if they are a pair of old-fashioned women's little feet.

In my hometown, little foot beans are like the aniseed beans written about by Mr. Lu Xun in Kong Yiji, a type of snack to eat with wine. But they are more eye-catching than aniseed beans. The pointed little packages are stacked high in the plate, which is not only exciting for people drinking wine, but can also elicit saliva from children.

When I was young, I often bought little foot beans to eat. At that time, they only cost one cent per package, and one copper coin could buy ten packages. Usually, one copper coin had to be divided into three or four purchases, buying three or four packages first and getting six or seven coins in change, then buying three or four packages again several times. But there were also times when I spent the whole copper coin and filled my pockets.

When I came home from school around noon or evening, my stomach was already empty. It tasted best to buy little foot beans to eat on the way. But before going to school, I would first buy them on the way and hide them in my pocket. When I was hungry in class, I would secretly open the straw paper package and put them into my mouth one by one, which was also a special taste.

From my house to school, I had to go through a long alley called Bridge Alley. There was a tavern in the middle of Bridge Alley that also sold little foot beans. The people running the tavern were a father and son: an old man and a middle-aged man. Everyone called it "Ah Lan's tavern," but no one knew whether it referred to the old man or the middle-aged man, or whether the character Lan in Ah Lan was written this way. But since I left my hometown, I have often recalled the living conditions of my childhood by chance, and associated them with the little foot beans of Ah Lan's tavern. Sometimes, I have also associated the various aspects of childhood life from the little foot beans. Especially in the past few years in Hangzhou, because I occasionally encountered the children from Ah Lan's tavern—who had grown into youths, with thin, white faces and pointed chins; if Ah Lan originally referred to the old man at that time, then this must be Ah Lan's grandson—I would often think of the little foot beans.

Lately, the more difficult my life has become, the more I have easily thought of the little foot beans—in my life history, the years of eating little foot beans can truly be considered a "golden age." Last time I returned to my hometown, I had already anticipated that I would very much like to eat little foot beans again and review the interests of childhood life. Although Ah Lan's tavern was still open there, and there were still pointed packages of little foot beans stacked high in the plate, various signs of decline at home dispelled my thoughts in the air. In fact, even if I insisted on buying little foot beans, I would not get the fun of those years, because I could no longer go to the classroom in school and touch them one by one. Although this taste is "gone for me," the nephews and nieces who are in their childhood should enjoy it properly. But according to my third brother, because the harvest is poor and taxes are heavy, the schools in my hometown are still suspended. Children don't even have a place to study, so there's no way to talk about the taste of eating little foot beans.

Five Years Later 235

— Ding

Such things are not uncommon. In books, in friends' casual chatter, in many situations, I often see and hear them. However, when it comes to experiencing it myself, it's different.

The matter is like this: One evening, as I was passing the entrance of the Great World, I was suddenly stopped by a woman who shouted in a worn-out voice, "Brother Ying, Brother Ying! Oh... where are you going? I haven't seen you in so long."

I looked up and saw a pale face, filled with a kind of life's bitterness and misfortune! Her eyes silently held unbearable sorrowful tears, staring blankly at me. I also stared blankly at her for a while. In my memory, I seemed to have seen such a woman before. However, even after strong searching, I still couldn't remember who she was.

"Forgotten? Brother Ying! Yes... yes, you wouldn't keep someone like me in your heart, oh... Brother Ying. You should remember me, ah, don't you really remember me at all?" She clung tightly to my side, trembling. I saw her chest rising and falling rapidly.

"Ah... really, I'm sorry, I forgot. Who are you? Tell me."

"Zhu Guifang... your classmate, a good friend five years ago," she said directly.

"Ah... you... are you Zhu Guifang? You... really are... Zhu Guifang? No... don't lie to me!" I was suddenly bewildered by this unexpected event.

At this time, the bystanders standing around us looked at us with curious eyes, and some even laughed out loud.

My face felt as if it had been烤 over fire, and my heart was in disarray.

She then dragged me along, saying:

"Brother Ying, let's go to my place and talk. There are too many people here, it's not convenient, and you're embarrassed!" She wasn't as desolate as before. When she spoke to me in that gentle tone, in her smiling coquettishness, I indeed remembered her previous attitude.

"Ah! Guifang..." I sighed, my heart feeling as if it had been pierced by a white blade.

"Don't worry, Brother Ying! As long as you... can... can remember me... someone like me... I'll... I'll be grateful to you."

"Life is truly ever-changing!" I said with emotion.

She looked at me, and a kind of unfortunate sorrow repeatedly shrouded her face. I didn't say anything more, lest I make her sad. So we walked in silence. She held my hand tightly, clinging tightly to my side.

"We're here, Brother Ying. This is my home..." Standing in the alley, she said.

"This is your home?" I questioned. I looked at the light hanging at the entrance, a white porcelain shade with red oil characters: "Guifen."

After a deep sigh, I followed her into her room.

"Please sit, Brother Ying. Let me tell you. You must be very surprised, right? Naturally, you wouldn't have imagined that Guifang would end up in this situation!"

"What's going on? Alas!..."

"Nothing else, Brother Ying, this isn't what I wanted either. Who would want this? But... it's really a last resort! A person, especially a woman without support, a woman without a father, a woman without opportunities for advancement, a woman without money to support her elderly mother in her sixties or seventies, like me! Besides trying to find some money, what other options are there? I need to live, my mother needs to live, my younger siblings need to live, my burden is heavy, my responsibility is great, I have to find a way to live. I've done everything, office worker, maid, factory worker. Brother Ying, you know my family situation, you also understand my personal character and behavior, didn't you once say to me?... 'Guifang... you are a capable person, intelligent, hardworking, and of good character, your future is limitless, you are an outstanding and promising woman...' However, Brother Ying! Those words only made me resentful and sad. People are completely controlled by their environment, like me, a fragile woman. In these four or five years, I've suffered enough of all kinds of torments and hardships... I've given up on this life. But, Brother Ying, you must understand me, understand me, and for me, speak to the world, to society, and to all our acquaintances, explain my situation, my misfortune, especially this kind of sin that I've committed!"

Then she began to sob.

Mr. Juqing (4) 236

— Ke Ling

In order to cope with these difficulties, Mr. Juqing had to carefully change the textbooks in the private school. Those thread-bound and stone-printed commercial application letter models, and even Western-style vernacular textbooks that were awkward to recite, entered the door and accompanied "Elementary Learning," "Mencius," and so on. Doing such things made Mr. Juqing as sad as a widow who had lost her chastity when trying to build a memorial arch. Vernacular Chinese was something he had always despised. Moreover, his only source of pride in his superior position among the many tutors in the town was that he could teach "Confucius said" and "The Book of Songs."

However, everything was irreversible. Just like the date of opening the school this first month of the year, he had no choice but to follow the trend and start early. Because of opening the school, he was nervously busy for several days beforehand. Madam Juqing, who was not often seen on the street, also squinted her old, near-sighted eyes and hobbled around the street on her small feet, informing the students of the start of school. Mr. Juqing himself was even more like a soldier charging to the front line, anxiously preoccupied, thinking about the opening of the school even while eating and sleeping. He wanted to use his own efforts to reverse a little of the current misfortune.

That day, Mr. Juqing met Mr. Tang, the father of student Tang Jialu, a self-cultivating farmer in the town in not-so-bad circumstances. Measuring the seven- or eight-year-old child next to Mr. Tang, Mr. Juqing squeezed out a little smile on his triangular face and began to chat with him:

"This is your son, how old is he?" Touching the child's shaved head.

"Seven years old after the new year, sir," he replied respectfully.

"Oh, very obedient!"

He nodded repeatedly, seeming to sincerely praise him. In his heart, he was considering how to put forward his main point tactfully. After hesitating for a while, he finally said, "You can send him to school, Mr. Tang." After saying that, his sunken eyes stared fixedly, waiting for a reply.

Mr. Tang smiled, a bitter smile.

"Yes, sir, he should be going to school according to his age. But 'water inlet' (note) is tight, and it's hard to make a living. Our farmers' annual harvest, after paying taxes and grain, isn't even enough to eat. We have to put aside the matter of the children's schooling. The district office added an education donation last year, saying it was for the school's expenses. It's still a farmer's child going to school, isn't it going to 'charge money' (note)!"

Listening to Mr. Tang's complaints, Mr. Juqing's heart turned cold. Looking at his purplish-red face, a large pile of wrinkles squeezed up, and the awkward expression that was like a smile but not a smile, it seemed that there were still many hardships he hadn't finished complaining about. He continued:

"Sir! I was originally planning to go to your residence these two days. Yesterday, the teacher's wife came to my house to notify me about the opening of the school, but I wasn't home, so I didn't tell her... (stopped for a moment) In recent years, our Jialu has been well taught by Mr. Yan, and he should study hard for a few more years to find a good business. But there are few people in the family, and it's expensive to hire a long-term worker, and they eat a lot, so... so, this year our Jialu has no choice but to drop his books and stay at home to help with the work."

Every word vibrated in Mr. Juqing's eardrums, buzzing like thunder. He was stunned and didn't open his mouth, and he almost didn't fall down.

(Note) "Water inlet" means "times" and "book money" means "tuition."

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Anglo-Russian Talks and China 237

— Li Min

The leader of a Western imperialist power, the British Empire, and a socialist country, the Soviet Union, have recently started negotiations between the two countries in Moscow by their respective representatives. This is a very important international event. Britain is the oldest empire in the West, while the Soviet Union is another country with a political system that is absolutely opposite to Britain. These two countries have always been in a position of irreconcilable conflict in international politics, but now they have actually begun to join hands for talks. What an interesting thing this is.

However, this is not surprising. Although Britain is an old empire in the West and has always opposed the Soviet Union, recently, due to the rise of Germany and its automatic rearmament, Britain is unable to control this chaotic European situation. On the other hand, Russia's power in Europe is increasing day by day, having reconciled with France and contacted various small countries. The United States, far away in the Americas, also restored diplomatic relations with the Soviet Union last year. Under this situation, the British Empire has no choice but to turn around and befriend this strange country in Europe in order to maintain its hegemony in Europe. This is a major reason why Britain is willing to send representatives to Moscow to talk with Russia. Russia needs all countries to reconcile with it and not attack it, so it is naturally more than welcoming Britain's willingness to come.

The world situation is truly ever-changing. In the few years after the European War - and even more so now - all countries hated this revolutionary Russia. However, in less than ten years, since two or three years ago, all countries have turned around and become close to Russia. This is enough for our country to reflect on. Naturally, the reason for this is that, on the one hand, the weak country of the past has now become a strong country, and on the other hand, the situation has created a force that can tip the scales. Therefore, countries with completely different ideologies also have a tendency to cooperate in the same boat. From this point of view, international affairs are nothing more than a pursuit of interests.

What is most noteworthy is the China issue. According to the news reports, these Anglo-Russian talks may touch upon the issue of China's territorial integrity. I don't know what their opinions on this issue are, and how they will discuss it? I am not in a position to predict it at this time, but in short, this is also in their interests and certainly not in our country's interests.

Zilu Asks the Way 238

— Erlang

Confucius left the state of Ye and was about to return to the state of Cai. On the way, he saw two people, Chang Ju and Jie Ni, plowing the field side by side. Confucius was very surprised and thought, "These two people are probably hermits." It happened that the disciple walking in front ran back and said, "There are two roads ahead, and I don't know which one is the right way to Cai. Please ask the teacher, should we go left or right?" Confucius didn't know either, and thought, "What should I do?" He instructed Zilu, "Zhong You, go and ask the people in the field." Zilu took the order and went, stood on the edge of the field, and respectfully asked Chang Ju and Jie Ni, "Excuse me, we want to go to the state of Cai, there are two roads ahead, and I don't know whether to go left or right?" Chang Ju and Jie Ni stopped plowing upon hearing this. Chang Ju glanced at Zilu and said, "Who is the one sitting in the carriage?" Zilu said, "It's Mr. Kong Qiu." He asked again, "Is it Kong Qiu of the state of Lu?" Zilu nodded and said, "Yes, that's right." Chang Ju laughed loudly and said, "Since it's him, then he knows the way." Jie Ni asked, "Who are you?" Zilu said, "My surname is Shen, and my name is You." He scrutinized him for a while and said, "Are you a disciple of Kong Qiu?" Zilu nodded, already very unhappy. Jie Ni said contemptuously, "There are so many people who are drunk and dreaming! But who is the savior?... Moreover, it is better to follow those who do not talk about politics than to follow those who study politics?" After saying that, he ignored Zilu, and the two of them continued to plow the field. Zilu stood there, thinking that these two people were really rude. He asked them the way sincerely, but after saying a few words, they also mocked him! It's okay if you don't tell me the way, why do you have to mock me, you bastards, I'll beat you up!" Confucius saw from afar that Chang Ju and Jie Ni ignored Zilu, and Zilu was standing on the edge of the field, clenching his fists and rubbing his palms, looking like he was about to use force, so he hurriedly called a disciple to pull Zilu back. Confucius frowned and asked, "Zhong You, what's wrong?" Zilu told Confucius everything about his conversation with Chang Ju and Jie Ni. Confucius sighed and said, "How can people be with animals? If the world is peaceful, I will not talk about politics."

One day, Zilu fell behind, feeling very anxious, and didn't know where Confucius's carriage had gone. He met an old man by the roadside, pulled him and asked, "Did you see the teacher?" The old man looked at Zilu and knew that he was a disciple of Kong Qiu. He sneered and said, "He doesn't work with his hands, and he doesn't know the five grains. How is he worthy of being a teacher?" Saying that, he stuck his cane in the edge of the field, got down into the field, and led the ox to plow the mud, ignoring him. Zilu had no choice but to find his own way. Unexpectedly, after walking not far and turning a bend, Confucius's carriage was parked under a large tree in front, resting. He hurried up and took long strides, and told Confucius what the old man had said, saying, "That old man is really hateful, he is scolding the teacher." Confucius lowered his eyebrows and thought for a while, "That's a hermit! What he said is right." Zilu thought that it would be very beneficial to go back and ask him some questions, and since he dared to say that their teacher was not worthy of being a teacher, then he must be more knowledgeable than their teacher. Without caring whether Confucius was happy or not, he turned around and ran back. But after turning a bend and running a long way, he was sweating all over. When he looked up, the old man was not plowing in the field, and he didn't know where he had gone.

Amateur Mailbox

The Production and Uses of Petroleum 239

Editor:

I am a high school graduate who gave up school to go into business due to economic difficulties, and since then, I have lost the opportunity to study. But because my knowledge base is too shallow, I cannot fully understand everything, especially natural sciences, which I find extremely vague. For example, I often see a lot of talk about "petroleum" in the newspaper, and I feel doubtful. I wonder, what is this petroleum? Is it gasoline? Is it kerosene? Is it another kind of oil?

I have asked many friends about this question, but they also don't know much about it, only telling me that it is a kind of oil extracted from minerals. They don't know if it is the same kind as gasoline.

I have a very annoying habit, which is that when I encounter a question, I must pursue it until I get to the bottom of it. Since others cannot satisfy my desire for knowledge, I have no choice but to bother you, sir. I think you will definitely be able to give me a clear explanation of it, right? But do you find me annoying? Sincerely,

Chang Zhilong respectfully

Editor's Note: Mr. Chang's habit of "breaking the clay pot to get to the bottom" is not a "bad" habit. It is a very helpful habit for learning. Nowadays, many people don't understand something, but they are unwilling to ask others because they are afraid of being laughed at. What a wrong mentality this is! Because no matter what, one can never understand everything in the world, and everyone naturally has things that they don't know. Therefore, asking others about questions that you don't know is not shameful, it is really a very good habit. I hope that everyone should have this kind of "questioning attitude". I think that the knowledge gained from others may be more valuable than the knowledge gained from reading books.

Petroleum is a general term for naphtha, commonly known as kerosene. It is a yellow or brown liquid, slightly transparent, with a certain

Page 18

odor, highly volatile, and easily flammable. Before the invention of gas lamps, petroleum was often used for lighting. Now, in addition to lighting, petroleum has other very important uses. It can operate petroleum-powered engines and gas-powered engines, for use in ships, cars, airplanes, and various industries. Military weapons such as airplanes and submarines require huge amounts of naphtha, so its position in military affairs is very important. At this time when there is a crisis of the outbreak of World War II, the competition for petroleum has become an important policy of various countries. The so-called "petroleum war" refers to this. Japan occupies our Eastern Provinces because there are abundant minerals such as naphtha and iron there, which can supply her with raw materials for war.

Naphtha is mostly hidden in new and old sedimentary rocks, or gushes out from mud volcanoes (volcanoes that erupt mud), and is accompanied by gases of hydrocarbons bursting out of volcanoes. As for the origin of naphtha, some say it is formed from inorganic solutions inside the earth, others say it comes from terrestrial plants. Recently, some have said that naphtha is formed from the fatty substances of organic matter, decomposed over a long period of time at relatively low temperatures. This seems to be a more credible explanation.

The mineral content of naphtha is too flammable, and it is not suitable for use in lamps. Usually, its volatility is utilized, and it is separated by distillation. The method is to put the crude oil extracted from the ground (which still has many viscous and black substances mixed in) into a蒸馏器heater, and the easily volatile part initially becomes steam and comes out. This steam is cooled and condensed, becoming volatile oil, which is used as fuel for automobiles, airplanes, submarines, and other machines. This is commonly known as gasoline. The next substance to evaporate at a slightly higher temperature is called lamp oil, which is commonly called kerosene, and is used in petroleum lamps and petroleum engines. The next substance to evaporate at an even higher temperature is called machine oil, which is used to lubricate axles and make them rotate smoothly. The next substance obtained is mineral fat, which is neither solid nor liquid, but a viscous substance in the crude oil, used to coat the surface of metals to prevent rust. Next is paraffin, used to make candles. What is left at the end is oil residue, called asphalt, used for roads, sand, and so on.

Based on existing estimates, the countries with the largest deposits of paraffin oil are the United States and Russia, accounting for about nine-tenths of the world's total. There is no accurate estimate of the production of paraffin oil mines in China, but it is probably very abundant. Its production areas are mostly in Xinjiang, Sichuan, Shaanxi, and other places. There are already more than a dozen oil wells being exploited, but most of the mining rights are controlled by foreign merchants. The outflow of rights and interests is really a matter that we should pay attention to.

Wang Bingmei of Donglai's Broad Deliberations

Hua Yu (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Qi, Lu, and Zheng Entering Xu (Continued)

Now offering it to Qi. But Qi dared not accept it. Offered it to Lu. Lu dared not accept it. Finally returning it to Zheng. Yet the Earl of Zheng still dared not sever the ancestral sacrifices of Xu. Marking off the borders of Xu. Alas. Who would say that the Spring and Autumn period was a time of contention and seizing, yet again seeing the style of virtue and yielding among the lords. Qi and Lu had no merit and dared not seize the merit of others. Zheng, although having merit, dared not hold onto their own merit. This is to be good at dealing with those without merit. Those like Qi and Lu. Good at dealing with those with merit. None surpass Zheng. This heart. How could it only be used in the midst of battlefields. Greatly sharing governance, and minutely sharing wealth. Extending this heart and residing in it, one will not fail to find contentment wherever they go. (End)

Marquis of Xi Attacks Zheng

Residing in lowliness, hating labor. Residing in poverty, hating hardship. Residing in difficulty, hating humiliation. All are the causes of disaster. The principle of the world. Lowliness does not seek labor, yet labor arrives on its own. Poverty does not seek hardship, yet hardship arrives on its own. Difficulty does not seek humiliation, yet humiliation arrives on its own. Not knowing that they cannot be separated and wanting to separate them. This is throwing oneself into disaster. The virtuous consider labor to be the constant of lowliness. Hardship is the constant of poverty. Humiliation is the constant of difficulty. That which makes them brave disaster is merely not being able to abide by their constant. If one abides in labor oneself, then one will be at peace in lowliness. If one abides in hardship oneself, then one will be at peace in poverty. If one abides in humiliation oneself, then one will be at peace in difficulty. The way of residing in a small country is also like this.

Supplement to the Local Edition of Shen Bao Movie Special

Helen Hayes' Childhood Reflected Through Her Beloved Daughter, Manley 245

— Renqin

Helen Hayes' name seems to need no introduction. What I want to introduce now is her beloved daughter, Manley. Manley is only five years old now and doesn't yet understand that she is fortunate to be the daughter of a big star, enjoying days of play. She's like a little Dutch girl, with two honey-yellow braids hanging over her shoulders. Her little mouth is red, and it is expected to stir the hearts of many young people in the future.

Helen Hayes is a big star who is both on stage and on screen, but because she herself has been acting since childhood and has not enjoyed the family happiness that children should enjoy, she now values family more than others. Her love for her Manley is self-evident. Helen Hayes' body does not belong to herself. It belongs to the vast audience, her husband, her mother, but the largest part belongs to her beloved daughter, Manley.

Once, a reporter went to visit Helen, but she unintentionally encountered Manley, which made her visit very rewarding. Manley ran in from outside, covered in mud. She entered the house! and sat on the floor in the middle of the room, starting to take off her shoes and socks. A dog ran over, sticking out its long tongue and licking her face, nose, and ears, expressing its welcome to the little master. At this moment, Manley began to murmur. She said, "I bought this for Christmas because my Michael is gone. He likes to lick my face, which makes me have to wash it several times, I mean wash my face several times, because you know, after a dog licks you, your face has a dog smell. You say it's okay not to wash it?" This long little speech made her breathless. So she had to laugh to herself, revealing her two dimples. Isn't this the reporter's unexpected gain?

At this moment, Helen had already walked in. Her youth and beauty were still evident, even though she was already a wife. "Whatever

Readers should note that Helen Hayes' performing life began at the age of five. She said, "My entry into the theater world is similar to Xiao Lidan's entry into the film industry now. My mother sent me to a dance school, telling me to get some good posture, as well as having an ingrown toe, and the doctor said that dancing could correct it. It was at the school's seasonal public performance, which was held by renting a theater, that I was seen by a big shot in the theater world. That was the beginning of my theatrical life. I was only five years old at the time, the same age as Manley is now.

"Manley is the same age as I was then, but whether she has a performing tendency and whether she will be an actress in the future is not something I'm concerned about at all. Although she is now enjoying a leisurely life, she may not be able to get all the fun that I went through before, or her life may not be as comprehensive as mine. But I don't want to see the god of destiny pointing Manley to her future. I am waiting for the natural order of things.

"I myself have been running around since I was a child, as the saying goes, growing up in a suitcase. According to child psychologists, children should be moved from place to place from time to time so that they can be lively, adaptable, make new friends, and be independent, not relying on others and not being afraid of difficulties. This may be true. But I may be a bit old-fashioned because I want Manley to have a stable life, which is also what I didn't enjoy when I was young.

A stable life, indeed, is what Helen Hayes has not enjoyed in her life and has been seeking day and night. Since the age of five, she has belonged to the public and has rarely enjoyed personal happiness, because the life of an actor is probably like this. Therefore, she said with emotion: "I am impatiently waiting for the time when I can retire and step into that sweet period called old age. Both my husband and I are looking forward to the arrival of old age. When that time comes, Keith (Helen's husband) will find a ridiculous photo and say, 'Let's hang this photo up. Manley's boyfriend will laugh to death when he sees it. At that time, wrinkled skin and white hair, old bear waddling; life's troubles, all become the past, the sunset years, are truly precious.'"

Movie Reviews

Review of "Rumba" 246

— Chan Fei

Rumba—Great Light

Among the usual song and dance films, this "Rumba" cannot but be called an outstanding work.

Although its content is inevitably mundane, merely a contrived fabrication of love material, the playwright has used well-versed film expression methods, making the emotional twists and turns between the male and female protagonists constitute a tortuous and bizarre narrative. From a new perspective, there is nothing particularly commendable, but for general audiences who need entertainment, it can make them feel satisfied. When the male and female protagonists meet for the first time while cashing lottery tickets, small conflicts arise. At the second meeting, the female protagonist is well-intentioned, but the male protagonist misunderstands and conflicts again, even causing him to lose his job. The third time, the male protagonist teaches the female protagonist a new dance technique, whispering intimately in the middle of the night, but she refuses to be any more unrestrained, causing him to become angry, even leading to another misunderstanding. The fourth time, the female protagonist goes to the male protagonist, originally to discuss marriage with great affection, but unbeknownst to her, the man has an ulterior motive. When sweet words and honeyed phrases and suspicions all disappear, another comes , (she is purposefully invited by the male protagonist for revenge.) Again, they are separated. Afterwards, the female protagonist passively returns home, and the male protagonist visits several times, but she ignores him, even though her love and hate are very conflicting and contradictory. All the way to the critical moment of life and death, the male and female protagonists finally truly fall in love in passionate dancing. With such a wavy plot, even this ordinary love dispute becomes extraordinary. The playwright's such rigorous structural power is indeed the highest expression of American love films.

What is even more noteworthy is the director's skill. At the beginning of the film, there are such extraordinary and lively shots, such a rapid tempo, expressing people's enthusiasm for lottery tickets. The same technique is used to handle the large-scale Rumba dance in the Cuban countryside, from monotonous to complex, from slow to fast, and finally extremely short CuttoCtu, complexly and chaotically weaving into a frenzied picture. Moreover, the enthusiastic music helps the enthusiasm and thickness of the air, which gives people a great interest in the enthusiastic customs of Cuba.

We must specifically mention the final Rumba dance on stage. He first used close-ups of many instruments, the conductor's caution and seriousness, arousing the audience's serious attention to the music. Then slowly the curtain opens, such a beautiful national case of the setting, such dim lighting, when people dragging shackles painful moaning out scene Several times the lightning flashes, the wind blowing the leaves tremble. As for the dance team of two women and one man, taking the stage together, the graceful dance poses, the passionate whispers of love, and the intoxicating music, everyone is intoxicated by it. All the way to the male and female protagonists embracing and taking the stage, in the midst of urgent feelings (because of worrying about the gangster's shooting) and passionate love, they successfully completed a brilliant scene. In this kind of place, we certainly will not ignore the efforts of the song and dance director and the composer, but the credit for the composition of the atmosphere cannot but be given to the general director.

In addition, we can also cite a few points to illustrate the director's proficiency; when the male protagonist meets the Cuban girl Camelia Tai, the director first uses another girl singing with the sound of the piano to describe the local scenery, and then from buying a three-dollar fan for five corners to attending the night dance, the humor of the time and the process of their acquaintance are all excellently handled. When the male and female protagonists dance late at night, the psychological depiction between the two can also be said to be extremely delicate. Therefore, this film, just in terms of the director, has already given us many good points.

Before, George Raft often played strong-character roles, but here, he appears with excellent dancing skills and unrestrained posture. As for Carole Lombard, we will not forget her hard work in "Twentieth Century Express," she is also suitable for playing strong-character actors. But what we like even more is Margo, who once showed her face in Peng Hequ's "Love in the Web," (Margo) The first time we meet her, she is a sincere and melancholy girl. She is passionately in love with a sinister lawyer, (Klaude Laines—CandeRainde as, namely the protagonist of "Battlefield Departure") When her lover abandons her, she is willing to sacrifice herself. In that film, we began to pay close attention to her, because her tone and posture were very outstanding. But it also feels that she is a bit too young, and the identity of the character in the play seems not very appropriate. Now she is appearing in "Rumba" again with the same posture. Although there are not many roles here, and she cannot give her full performance, she can indeed make people recognize that she has a great future.

However, it is a pity that so many excellent talents are gathered in this film, but they have not expressed a more commendable theme. Here, in addition to the conventional depiction of the love disputes between men and women, they are engaged in the exaggeration of form with the greatest strength. It is very obvious that from the male protagonist, the playwright's old-fashioned ideas are being expressed. We do not say that his departure from the life of a gangster is not appropriate, but his striving to go upstream and then combine with a rich girl, this just shows that the upward climbing of the gentleman's concept is ultimately vulgar.

Shen Bao Architecture Weekly

The Construction of Affordable Housing (Part 1) 248

— Xi Hao

…Points to Note…

The construction of affordable housing, after the Municipal Government's vigorous advocacy, will commence shortly. This is truly encouraging and fortunate for every commoner. It is a construction worthy of our admiration. Of course, for these new buildings, we do not hope they will be magnificent and luxurious, but at least we hope that they will be as well-equipped as possible within the feasible range. From what I can see, the following points must be given special attention before designing these new houses.

(1) Hygiene Problems—The most lacking facility in past commoner residences was hygiene. The low houses, with windows of less than one square foot opened on the walls, the damp mud ground, and the dark walls, were filled with foul odors. They simply did not resemble houses fit for human habitation. Furthermore, there were no toilet facilities. As a result, the surroundings of the houses were always full of excrement. All of this not only harmed the health of the residents but also affected passers-by, neighbors, and even the entire area. Therefore, when we design new houses, the first and most important thing to consider is hygiene. The most crucial thing is ventilation. The area of the windows must be appropriate to allow the air in the room to circulate as much as possible. The material for the floor should preferably be wooden or concrete, striving to be easy to sweep or clean. Toilet facilities are truly the most important. These toilets must be convenient and easy to clean. At the same time, in addition to private toilets, several public toilets should be set up, and their locations should be central.

Bathroom facilities seem to have been overlooked by every engineer in affordable housing. This is a great mistake. Bathing is truly the biggest problem in hygiene, especially for ordinary laborers who work hard all day long. Returning home covered in coal ash, if they could have a quick bath, it would be of great benefit to their health, especially during the summer when epidemics occur, which can be greatly reduced. Therefore, every house should have a bathroom. Such a bathroom can be very simple, for example, just a bathtub and a tap. Hot water can be supplied by themselves. However, the drainage of bathwater must have very convenient gutters, and this must be noted.

(2) Safety Issues—The most common danger in densely populated cities is fire. In the past, affordable housing, due to its interconnected nature, would spread rapidly once a fire broke out, making it impossible to rescue. We can see in the newspapers at any time that the number of commoners who perish in fire pits every year is considerable. The reason for this fire is mostly due to carelessness in using "portable stoves" or "wind stoves" for cooking. Most commoners have a difficult life and cannot afford to build a stove, so they have to use cheap substitutes such as "portable stoves." The application of these things is improper, and the danger is very great because they do not have ventilation chimneys. Therefore, in the new houses, each family should have a stove built for them in advance (a pot stove is sufficient).

Changes in Social Life and Architectural Styles 249

— Translated by Zhang Guangzheng from the Japanese of Taniguchi Chusaku

Architectural style is one of the symbols of the culture of an era, but it is also greatly influenced by materials.

The original materials of architecture were natural stone and natural trees, thus possessing their special styles. In places such as Egypt, Greece, and Rome, relying on the utilization of produced marble, beautiful marble buildings were built. The art of architecture was accepted, and its style was determined. This style is the main source of European architectural styles. This is called the architectural style of stone material utilization.

Conversely, in Japan, where forests are abundant and there are earthquakes, stone buildings are not developed, and natural wooden buildings have risen instead. The architectural style of Japan is a wooden utilization style.

Without special scientific treatment, but only utilizing the styles of natural wood and stone, the construction method is naturally extremely simple.

However, since the Industrial Revolution in the nineteenth century, scientific advancements have been rapid, and building materials have also been greatly affected. Because of the production of iron, cement, glass, etc., the simple architectural structure style of utilizing natural objects alone has been fundamentally changed. Due to the utilization of iron and cement, the steel frame structure replaced the old shield structure.

On the one hand, due to the research of mechanics, rational mechanical design has been applied to architectural structures. In the past, the huge, oversized columns and overly thick walls of stone and brick structures have been reduced to a certain extent, and the number of floors has been increased. The space occupied by the structural material parts of buildings has been reduced, becoming a style that utilizes vast space.

Moreover, buildings utilizing iron and cement are also earthquake-resistant, fire-resistant, and wind-resistant. The architectural style of utilizing natural stone and natural trees in the past, even if it is superior in art, is far inferior to the style of utilizing iron and cement in terms of practicality.

However, architecture is not satisfactory if it only meets practical needs. Therefore, various materials for decorating iron and cement have been scientifically researched. For example, for the beauty of the exterior, there is artificial marble; for indoor insulation, soundproofing, and beautiful materials, fiberboard, gypsum board, and wood veneers are used.

Today, the iron and cement machinery is not only practical, but also beautified by the production of various decorative materials. However, in the future, there will be a further requirement, that is, the research of materials suitable for hygienic equipment such as air washing, heating, soundproofing, and moisture-proofing, which cannot be delayed any longer.

In this way, on the one hand, buildings are containers for human life; on the other hand, the power of advancing science is used to satisfy the infinite desires of mankind. However, construction costs and equipment costs will inevitably increase further. The resulting result is that the difference between the poor and the rich in buildings becomes more and more obvious. This is an important social issue and cannot be ignored. Therefore, in addition to the research on building materials suitable for the magnificent and luxurious architecture of iron and cement, equally important is the research on new materials that are more affordable and have the purpose of resistance to moisture, earthquakes, and fire, in addition to iron and cement, for the lives of ordinary people, which is a necessary point in the research of building materials in the future. However, the supply of excellent building materials at low prices requires the unification of architectural styles. With a certain type of material, factories can then produce in large quantities. In Germany, the sizes of various parts of houses, windows, doors, etc., are unified in two or three types. That is, the architectural style is gradually tending towards simplification.

The famous material of a certain model of house is produced in large quantities by factories. When building a house, assembling and combining according to the drawings, this method is the shortcut to obtaining the cheapest and most beautiful house.

For this reason, the general public and architects should be aware. For the sake of everyone's livelihood, they should sacrifice their personal desires, not adhere to special architectural styles, but be satisfied with architectural styles that utilize unified materials.

If so, excellent buildings will be much cheaper than now, and the shortening of the construction period is even more unexpected. Relying on this, the damage of large earthquakes and theft can be reduced; and daily life can be made more hygienic. Then, health and economic conditions will also inevitably improve day by day.

I hope that people can understand this point as soon as possible, and that the needs and the architects can be satisfied with the architectural style obtained by using unified materials.

The Science of Building Materials (8) 250

— Zhu Zhenmu

(4) Sulfur - Sulfur is very active. If it combines with iron in steel, it can form iron sulfide, which is a poor quality product that reduces strength and toughness. If it combines with magnesium in iron to form magnesium sulfide, it easily rusts the steel. Not only this, but steel with high sulfur content becomes brittle when heated to red hot. Therefore, it is only suitable to be 0.05 percent long, and beyond this, it is greatly disadvantageous.

(5) Mirror quality - Manganese is also easy to make steel hard, so it is only suitable to contain 0.4 to 0.72 percent. If the manganese content in steel exceeds 0.7 percent, its hardness will make it difficult for blacksmiths to work, and if it exceeds 12 percent, it can only be used as tools such as chisel stones and cannot be used for other purposes.

(6) Aluminum - Aluminum is a gasification barrier that can make steel rust-free and can reduce weight, but it is limited to a maximum of 0.05 percent. Beyond this, there is a risk of combining with carbon to form graphite. Aluminum steel is sold on the market, which is this.

(7) Chromium - The addition of chromium to steel can obtain great strength. There is a thing called "anti-force and great strength" on the market, which is this kind of chromium steel material. Its composition is best not to exceed 13 to 18 percent.

(8) Vanadium - Vanadium can also make steel strong and tough. It is mostly used in advanced industrial manufacturing, such as springs and axles, which are the best quality steel materials. However, the value is extremely high.

(9) In steel - When the quality in steel reaches 3.5%, it can make it strong and durable, and when it is 36%, it can be insensitive to strong temperature, so in the construction industry, it is used as a measuring ruler to make it accurate and unchanged, also known as non-expanding steel.

Section 2 Rust

In steel problems, rust is a very big difficulty, because after the pot iron rusts, it not only damages the force energy, but also reduces the beauty. As for the reason why it rusts, it should be explained by the two theories of being oxidized or thundered, but due to the relationship of space, I will not say more: the steel contains sulfur and manganese, which is more likely to rust.

The methods of preventing rust are no more than the following.

(1) Paint - Painting on iron can isolate it from the humid air outside, thereby preventing rust. However, the paint is easy to fall off, so it must be repainted every year to be cautious.

(2) Cement - Wrap the steel bone with two inches thick of cement aggregate, which can protect it every time.

(3) Pure steel - If the steel is refined purely, it will not rust. (To be continued)
